النفس مالها وما عليها (۲) دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ تعریف تھی میں لفظ نقہ نہ ذکر کیا جائے فقط اس کی تفسیر ذکر کی جائے عبارت یوں ہوگی ھو علم بقواعد التي يتوصل بها الى معرفة النفس مالها وما عليها اول صورت مردود ہے کیونکہ اس میں طول بلا سود ہے ثانی صورت اگر چہ قابل قبول ہے لیکن اس میں وہی تکرار والی خرابی لازم آتی ہے کیونکہ ایک مرتبہ تو یہاں فقہ کی تعریف ہوگی پھر جب حد اضافی کی جائے گی تو اس میں دوبارہ فقہ کی تعریف کرنی پڑے گی اس لئے کہ الفقہ مضاف الیہ ہے حد اضافی یہ ہے کہ مضاف اور مضاف الیہ کی علیحدہ تعریف کی جائے تو بحیثیت مضاف الیہ ہونے کے فقہ کی دوبارہ تعریف کرنی پڑے گی تو تکرار محض لازم آئے گا جس طرح کہ علامہ ابن حاجب نے اپنی کتاب الاضول میں ایسا ہی کیا ہے لیکن اگر تعریف اضافی کو مقدم کیا جائے تو تکرار والی خرابی لازم نہیں آئے گی کیونکہ فقہ کی تعریف مفصلاً اس میں آجائے گی بعدہ حدیقی میں صرف الفقہ کا لفظ ذکر کر دینا کافی ہو گا تعریف کی ضرورت نہیں ہوگی طالب الفقہ کرد علم پہلے ہی تعریف جان چکا ہوگا۔ گروہ ثانی بھی دو دلیلیں بیان کرتا ہے (۱) دلیل اول یہ ہے کہ اصول فقہ اب علم بن چکا ہے اس فن کا اور اعلام میں مقصود معنی علمی ہوا کرتا ہے اور حدیقی میں بھی معنی علمی بیان کیا جاتا ہے لہذا اس کو مقدم ہونا چاہیے اضافی پر جو که غیر مقصود ہے (۲) دلیل دوم یہ ہے کہ حد اضافی بمنزلہ مرکب کے ہے اور حالتی بمنزلہ بسیط کے ہے اور ، ضابطہ ہے البسيط مقدم على المركب البذا جو بمنزلہ بسیط ہے وہ بھی مقدم ہوگا بمنزلہ مرکب پر اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ حد لقمی مقدم علی الاضافی ہوگی۔
The self, what is for it and against it (2) The second form is that in the definition, the word fiqh is not mentioned, only its explanation is given. The phrase would be: 'It is the knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at knowing what is for and against the self.' The first form is rejected because it has length without benefit. The second form, although acceptable, entails the same flaw of repetition because once here the definition of fiqh will occur, then when the added definition (hadd idafi) is made, the definition of fiqh will have to be given again. This is because 'fiqh' is the added-to (mudaf ilayh). The added definition is that the mudaf and mudaf ilayh are defined separately. So due to being mudaf ilayh, the definition of fiqh would be repeated, and pure repetition would necessarily occur, as Allama Ibn Hajib did in his book al-Usul. But if the added definition is presented first, then the flaw of repetition does not necessarily occur because the definition of fiqh will come in detail within it. Afterwards, in the laqabi definition, it is sufficient to just mention the word fiqh; there is no need for definition, as the student of fiqh already knows the definition. The second group also presents two proofs: (1) The first proof is that Usul al-Fiqh has become a science of this art, and in titles (a'lam) the intended meaning is the scientific meaning, and in the laqabi definition the scientific meaning is also expressed. Therefore, it should be given precedence over the added definition, which is not intended. (2) The second proof is that the added definition is like a compound, and the laqabi definition is like a simple. The principle is: the simple takes precedence over the compound. Therefore, what is like a simple will also take precedence over what is like a compound. From this it is proven that the laqabi definition takes precedence over the added definition.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute about the order of defining Usul al-Fiqh. Two groups are mentioned. The first group argues that if you define fiqh first (as in the first form), it leads to useless length; the second form (defining fiqh indirectly) is acceptable but leads to repetition if the added definition (hadd idafi) is given after. They suggest that the added definition should come first to avoid repetition. The second group gives two rational proofs (dalil aqli) for presenting the laqabi definition first: first, Usul al-Fiqh is now a science with a title, and titles carry scientific meanings; second, the laqabi definition is simpler (basiṭ) like a simple term, and the principle is that the simple precedes the compound. This is a classic Hanafi usul debate about methodology of definition. The text does not explicitly state which view is preferred, but the discussion sets the stage for the author's own approach.

Key Terms
حد اضافی (hadd idafi): Definition that considers the added relation between mudaf and mudaf ilayh; e.g., defining usul al-fiqh by separately defining usul and fiqh.
حد لقبی (hadd laqabi): Definition that treats the term as a title (laqab) indicating a specific science, without breaking it into parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second group, what is the main reason the laqabi definition should be presented first?
A) It avoids any repetition of the definition of fiqh.
B) It is simpler and conveys the scientific meaning intended in titles, and the simple takes precedence over the compound.
C) It is the method used by Ibn Hajib.
D) It includes a detailed definition of fiqh.

Key Takeaway
The order of definitions in usul al-fiqh reflects a methodological choice; the laqabi (title) definition is often placed first because it is simpler and conveys the scientific essence.

Literal vs Customary Meaning of Asl in Usul al-Fiqh
Analyzing the definition of 'asl' and its division into sensory and rational building

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the literal and customary definitions of 'asl' in usul al-fiqh and apply the Hanafi principle of avoiding naql to determine the intended meaning.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school defines 'asl' in 'usul al-fiqh' as 'rational foundation' (ibtina' aqli) by its literal meaning to avoid metaphorical transposition.

The term 'asl' is foundational to usul al-fiqh, but its exact meaning is debated: does it mean 'foundation' (literal) or 'evidence' (customary)? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position that prefers the literal meaning to avoid naql (metaphorical transposition), a principle rooted in the idea that original meanings are not abandoned without necessity. By examining the textual analysis in Misk al-Maleeh, you will learn how context (idafa to fiqh) resolves ambiguity and makes the intended meaning definitive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible meanings of 'asl'
Determine the literal meaning (foundation/building, ibtina') and the customary meaning (evidence, dalil).
The literal meaning has two subdivisions: sensory and rational building.
2
Understand the principle of naql
Recognize that transferring a word from its literal meaning (naql) is contrary to the original and not allowed without necessity.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle.
3
Analyze the Hanafi argument for the literal meaning
Note how the context of 'idafa to fiqh' specifies rational building, making the literal meaning definite without needing naql.
The addition to 'fiqh' (a rational discipline) restricts the meaning.
4
Evaluate the opposing argument for certainty
The opposing group claims the customary meaning is more certain. Understand their reasoning.
They argue that the literal meaning includes sensory building, which is unintended.
5
Trace the Hanafi rebuttal
The commentator al-Taftazani refutes the objection by showing that context eliminates uncertainty, so the literal meaning is equally definite.
The rebuttal also addresses a further objection about the nature of ibtina' itself.

مسک الملیح
شرح التوضيح والتلوي
ہمیں نقل ہوگی اور نقل خلاف الاصل ہے اور بلا ضرورت رجوع الی خلاف الاصل جائز نہیں لہذا اصلی معنی چھوڑ کر نعلی مراد نہیں لیا جائے گا پھر معنی اصلی والغوی کے دو فرد یا دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) ابناء حسی یعنی بنساء الشئى على الشئي حسا وظاهرا شارح نے اس کی تین مثالیں بیان کی ہیں (۱) ابتناء السقف على الجدران (جدران جمع جدا معنی دیوار ) (۲) ابتناء اعالى الجدار على الاساس دیوار کے اوپر والے حصے کا ابتنا نیچے والے حصے پر (۳) اغصان الشجر کی بناء على دوحته (بتہ ) ۔ دوسری قسم (۲) ابتناء عقلی یعنی ابتـنـاء الشئى على الشئي باعتبار العقل اس کی مثالیں (۱) ابتناء مجاز على الحقيقت (۲) ابتناء احكام جزئيه على القواعد الكليه (۳) ابتناء معلولات على العلل (۴) ابتناء مشتق على المشتق منه (۵) ابتناء حكم على الدليل مصنف نے صرف آخری مثال بیان کی ہے شارح نے بھی اسی کو ذ کر کیا ہے تو بقول مصنف یہاں اصول سے لغوی معنی مراد ہے یعنی ابتناء پھر ابتناء کی دو قسموں میں سے یہاں ابتناء عقلی مراد ہے ۔ سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ آپ کے پاس کیا قرینہ ہے کہ ابتناء سے ابتناء عقلی مراد ہے وبالاضافة الى الفقہ سے شارح قرینہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ اصول کی اضافت فقہ کی طرف ہے اور فقہ ایک علم کا نام ہے وہ ایک معنی عقلی و علمی ہے اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ اصل سے مراد اجتناء عقلی ہے پھر ابتنا عقلی کی صورتوں میں سے یہاں ابتناء الحکم علی دایلہ مراد ہے کیونکہ اصول فقہ کا معنی ہوگا وہ اشیاء جن پر فقہ مبنی ہو اور وہ اشیاء جو مستندالیہ بن رہی ہوں فقہ کے لئے اور علم کیلئے جو چیز منبعی علیہ اور مستند الیہ بنتی ہے وہ دلیل ہی ہوتی ہے تو اصول الفقہ کا معنی ہوگا ہو لائل الفقہ تو مصنف کے نزدیک بھی اصل بمعنی دلیل ہو گا لیکن با اعتبار معنی لغوی اور باعتبار ا سکے کہ دلیل ، اصل کے لغوی معنی کی دو قسموں میں سے ایک قسم ہے اور اسمیں نقل کا اعتبار نہیں ہو گا بخلاف گروہ ثانی کے وہ اصل بمعنی دلیل بناتے ہیں باعتبار مجاز کے اور اسمیں نقل کا ارتکاب کرنا پڑتا ہے۔ وبهذا يندفع ما يقال الخ اس عبارت سے شارح تفتازانی ایک اشکال ! کو دفع کر رہے ہیں جو کہ گروہ ثانی کی طرف سے مصنف پر وارد ہوتا ہے کہ اگر اصل کا عرفی معنی ، دلیل ، مراد لیا جائے تو وہ متعین متیقن ہے اور قطعا مقصود پر دلالت کرتا ہے اس میں غیر کا بالکل احتمال نہیں ہے اور اگو لغوی معنی مراد ہو تو یہ مقصود و غیر مقصود اور مرادونا مراد ( من مقولہ شیخ مولانا علی محمد نور اللہ مرقدہ ) دونوں کو شامل ہے اور مقصود پر دلالت کرنے میں مشکوک محتمل ہے کیونکہ مقصود صرف ابتباء عقلی ہے حالانکہ معنی لغوی ابتنا حسی کو بھی شامل ہے (جو غیر مقصود ہے لھذا معنی عرفی ہی مراد لینے چاہیں جو کہ یقینی اور قطعی ہے آپ شکی و احتمالی معنی کیوں مراد لیتے ہو ؟ جواب ! اس عبارت سے اس اشکال کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ہماری گذشتہ تقریر سے یہ اشکال رفع ہو گیا ہے وہ اس طرح کہ یہاں لغوی معنی ہی مراد ہے کیونکہ عرفی معنی مراد لینے میں مجاز اور نقل کا ارتکاب لازم آتا ہے جو کہ خلاف اصل ہے باقی رہا یہ اشکال کہ لغوی معنی محتمل ہے مقصود اور غیر

Misk al-Maleeh: Commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. We have (the issue of) naql (transposition), and naql is contrary to the original (asl), and without necessity, resorting to that which is contrary to the original is not permissible. Therefore, we do not leave the original meaning and take a transferred (naqli) meaning. Then the original and lexical meaning has two individuals or two types: (1) Sensory ibtina' (building): that is, the building of a thing upon a thing sensibly and apparently. The commentator (sharh) gave three examples: (a) the building of a roof upon walls, (b) the building of the upper part of a wall upon its foundation, (c) the building of tree branches upon its trunk. The second type: (2) Rational ibtina': that is, the building of a thing upon a thing by mental consideration. Its examples: (a) the building of metaphor upon reality, (b) the building of particular rulings upon general rules, (c) the building of effects upon causes, (d) the building of a derived word upon its base, (e) the building of a ruling upon its evidence. The author (musannif) mentioned only the last example, and the commentator also mentioned it. So according to the author, here the lexical meaning of 'asl' is intended, i.e., ibtina', then of the two types of ibtina', rational ibtina' is intended here. Question: What evidence do you have that rational ibtina' is intended from ibtina'? By (the phrase) 'and by relation to fiqh', the commentator is stating the evidence: that 'usul' is added to 'fiqh', and fiqh is the name of a knowledge, and it is a rational and intellectual meaning. From this it is established that the intended meaning of 'asl' is rational ibtina'. Then among the forms of rational ibtina', here the intention is the building of a ruling upon its evidence, because the meaning of 'usul al-fiqh' would be: the things upon which fiqh is built, and the things that become the basis for fiqh. And for knowledge, the thing that becomes the source and basis is the evidence (dalil). So the meaning of 'usul al-fiqh' is 'the evidences of fiqh'. So for the author as well, 'asl' has the meaning of 'dalil', but from the perspective of the lexical meaning and from the aspect that 'dalil' is one of the two types of the lexical meaning of 'asl', and in this there is no need for naql. Contrary to the second group, they make 'asl' mean 'dalil' from the perspective of metaphor, and in that they have to commit naql. 'And by this, what is said is repelled...' With this phrase, the commentator al-Taftazani is repelling an objection that comes from the second group against the author: that if the customary meaning of 'asl', i.e., 'dalil', is intended, then it is definite and certain and indicates the intended meaning absolutely, with no possibility of other. But if the lexical meaning is intended, then it includes both the intended and unintended, and is doubtful and probable in indicating the intended, because the intended is only rational ibtina', while the lexical meaning includes sensory ibtina' (which is unintended). Therefore, the customary meaning should be taken, which is certain and definitive. Why do you take a doubtful and probable meaning? Answer: With this phrase he is answering the objection, that our previous discussion has removed this objection. It is like this: here the lexical meaning is intended, because taking the customary meaning necessitates metaphor and transposition, which is against the original. As for the objection that the lexical meaning is probable and includes both intended and unintended, this is incorrect, because we have made clear that here from ibtina' only rational ibtina' can be intended, which is our intended meaning, because the addition of 'usul' to 'fiqh' specifies this meaning. When rational ibtina' is specified and it is our intended meaning, then the indication of 'asl' to this intended meaning is definitive, not probable, because the possibility of sensory ibtina' is completely removed. 'For if you say: ibtina' is the building of a thing upon a thing...' The purpose of commentator al-Taftazani is objection and answer. The objection is that the division of ibtina' into sensory and rational is baseless; rather, ibtina' is only rational. Because ibtina' is the name for the relation between the built thing (mabni) and the thing built upon (mabni 'alayh), and it is a masdar meaning, and masdar meaning is an abstract meaning, relational meaning, and rational meaning, which does not exist externally. Because the masdar meaning is from the category of relation, and relational things are non-existent externally, while sensory ibtina' requires external existence. So it is established that ibtina' is always rational and cannot be sensory. Then the division of ibtina' into sensory and rational would be a division of a thing into itself and something else, which is invalid. Answer: 'I say...' The commentator is answering that the division of ibtina' into sensory and rational is not with respect to ibtina' itself (which is a relational meaning), but rather with respect to the two sides, i.e., the two things (the builder and the built-upon). So sensory ibtina' means that the two sides are sensory, and rational ibtina' means that the two sides are rational. Therefore, the division is correct. Then for 'two sensory things' two meanings are given: (1) That the two things are sensory with respect to any of the five senses, whether eye or ear etc. But there is an objection to this meaning: just as the building of a roof upon a wall is included in sensory ibtina', similarly the building of a derived word upon its base (like the building of a verb upon its masdar) would also be included in sensory ibtina', because although it is not visible to the eye, it is audible to the ear, as 'shurb' and 'darb' are heard. Yet it is well-known that the building of a derived word upon its base is rational ibtina'. (2) The second meaning of sensory ibtina' is customary: that the two things are sensory by sight and eye, i.e., visually sensory. In common usage, 'sensory' means that which is observed by the eyes, that one thing is built upon another and placed. 'And thereby such examples are excluded...' Here also an objection arises: according to the customary meaning, the building of a derived word upon its base would be excluded from sensory ibtina', but the author's definition/interpretation of rational ibtina' as 'the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence' does not include the building of a derived word upon its base either, because the building of a derived word upon its base is not an ordering of a ruling upon its evidence. Yet it is well-known that the building of a derived word upon its base is included in rational ibtina'. 'And the truth is that the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence...' From here, commentator al-Taftazani is answering this objection: we adopt the second meaning (customary sensory) and take the customary meaning of 'sensory', and we include the building of a derived word upon its base in rational ibtina', because the correct view is that the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence is one example of rational ibtina', not the only one.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage from Misk al-Maleeh, a commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, addresses the definition of the term 'asl' in 'usul al-fiqh'. The debate centers on whether 'asl' should be taken in its literal (haqiqi) sense of 'foundation' (bina') or in its customary (urf) sense of 'evidence' (dalil). The author (the commentator) defends the literal interpretation. He begins by stating a general principle: transposition (naql) of a word from its original meaning is not allowed without necessity. Thus, we cannot abandon the literal meaning for a metaphorical one unless required. The literal meaning of 'asl' is 'building' (ibtina'), which has two types: sensory (hissi) and rational (aqli). Sensory building is when one thing is physically placed upon another, like a roof on walls. Rational building is when the relationship is intellectual, such as a ruling being built upon its evidence, a derivative upon its root, etc. The author asserts that in 'usul al-fiqh', the intended meaning is rational building, specifically the building of a ruling upon its evidence. This is because 'usul' is added to 'fiqh', and fiqh is a rational discipline; the things upon which fiqh is built are its evidences. Therefore, 'usul al-fiqh' means 'the evidences of fiqh'. Even though 'asl' in its literal sense includes both sensory and rational building, the context (idafa to fiqh) restricts it to rational building. The objection from the opposing group is that taking the literal meaning is uncertain because it includes sensory building which is not intended, whereas the customary meaning (dalil) is certain and definite. The author responds that the literal meaning is preferred because the customary meaning would require metaphorical transposition (naql), which is avoided. Moreover, the uncertainty is removed because the addition to fiqh specifies only rational building. Thus, the indication is definitive. The passage then addresses a further objection about the definition of ibtina' itself: it is argued that ibtina' is always rational because it is a relational masdar, not a physical entity. The commentator clarifies that the division into sensory and rational is not about ibtina' itself but about the two relata (the builder and the built-upon). Finally, two definitions of 'sensory' are discussed: one based on any of the five senses, and the other based on sight only (the customary definition). The latter is adopted to include only physical building and exclude derivatives, which are then included in rational building.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): Linguistically means 'foundation' (bina') upon which something is built; in usul al-fiqh, it means rational foundation, specifically evidence (dalil) without metaphorical transposition.
ابتناء (ibtina'): The act of building or basing; a relational concept between a builder and a thing built upon.
حسي (hissi): Pertaining to the senses; in this context, two definitions: (1) perceivable by any of the five senses, (2) perceivable by sight only (customary).
عقلي (aqli): Pertaining to the intellect; in this context, building that is not physical but based on rational relationship, e.g., ruling upon evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafi scholar in this passage prefers the literal meaning of 'asl' (foundation) over the customary meaning (evidence) for 'usul al-fiqh'?
A) Because the literal meaning is more precise and avoids doubt.
B) Because the customary meaning requires metaphorical transposition (naql), which is contrary to the original principle.
C) Because the literal meaning includes both sensory and rational building, making it more comprehensive.
D) Because the majority of scholars agree on the literal meaning.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines 'asl' in 'usul al-fiqh' as 'rational foundation' (ibtina' aqli) through its literal meaning, specified by context, to avoid unnecessary metaphorical transposition.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Division of Ibnā' into Sensory and Intellectual
Sharḥ al-Talwīḥ defending division of ibnā' against objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the division of ibnā' into sensory and intellectual is valid in Hanafi usul and distinguish between a definition and an example in textual analysis.

Core Idea
Ibnā' is divided by its terms, not the relation itself.

In this passage from Sharḥ al-Talwīḥ, the commentator Taftazani defends the division of ibnā' (resting/basing) into sensory and intellectual against an objection. The objection claims that ibnā' is purely intellectual because it is a relational concept. The response clarifies that the division is based on the two sides (based and base), not the relation. Furthermore, the author's phrase 'ordering of a ruling upon its evidence' is not a definition but an example, preserving the comprehensive scope of intellectual ibnā'. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying analogical reasoning (qiyās) in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and response
The objector claims ibnā' cannot be sensory because it is a relational (intellectual) meaning. The commentator responds that the division is based on the two terms, not the relation itself.
The relation is always intellectual; what can be sensory or intellectual are the things related.
2
Understand the basis of the division
Sensory ibnā' means the two things (mabnī and mabnī ʿalayhi) are sensory; intellectual ibnā' means they are intellectual. This refutes the objection.
The division is of the two sides, not the relation.
3
Distinguish the two meanings of 'sensory'
First meaning: any of the five senses (would include audible derivations, problematic). Second meaning: conventional, restricted to visual perception. The author adopts the second to exclude verbal derivation.
Convention (ʿurf) defines sensory as visually perceptible.
4
Recognize that the author's phrase is an example, not a definition
The phrase 'ordering of a ruling upon its evidence' is one particular instance of intellectual ibnā', not its definition. The true definition is 'resting of a thing upon a thing by consideration of the intellect'.
If taken as definition, it would exclude other valid forms like derivation of actions from verbal nouns.
5
Apply this principle to other examples
Intellectual ibnā' includes ordering of effects on causes, derivation of metaphor from literal, derivation of actions from sources, etc. This classification affects how one understands qiyās and istiḥsān.
The example does not limit the general rule.

فان قلت ابتناء پرقط الشئى على الشئى غرض شارح تفتازانی اعتراض و جواب ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ ابتناء کی تقسیم الی الحسی والعقلی باطل ہے بلکہ ابتنا، صرف عقلی ہوتا ہے کیونکہ ابتنا، نام ہے اس نسبت کا جو مبنی اور مبنی علیہ کے درمیان ہوتی ہے اور یہ ایک معنی مصدری ہے اور معنی مصدری معنی انتزاعی معنی اضافی اور معنی عقلی ہوتا ہے جو کہ موجود فی الخارج نہیں ہوتا اس لئے کہ معنی مصدری من قبیل الاضافہ ہوتا ہے اور ہو جائے گی وھو باطل جواب قلت سے شارح جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ تقسیم ابتنا الی الحسی و العقلی نفس ابتنا ء کے اعتبار سے نہیں ہے ( جو کہ ابتناء ایک معنی اضافی ہے) بلکہ تقسیم طرفین و شیمین یعنی مبنی اور مبنی درست ہے پھر کون الشیئین محسوسین کے دو معنی کیے گئے ہیں (۱) وہ شیمین محسوس ہوں کہ حواس خمسہ میں سے کسی ایک حاسہ کے ساتھ خواہ آنکھ ہو یا کان وغیرہ لیکن اس معنی پر اشکال ہوتا ہے کہ جس طرح ابتناء السقف على الجدار ابتنا حسی میں داخل ہے اسی طرح ابتناء المشتق على المشتق منہ ( ابتناء الفعل على المصدر ) یہ بھی ابتنا حسی میں داخل ہو جائے گا۔ اس لیئے کہ اگر چہ یہ محسوس با البصر نہیں ہے لیکن محسوس با اسمع تو ہے کہ شرب اور ضرب کو کان سنتے ہیں تو یہ بھی حاسہ پانچ میں داخل ہے حالانکہ مشہور تو یہ ہے کہ ابتناء المشتق على المشتق منہ ابتنا عقلی ہے (۲) دوسرا معنی ابتنا حسی کا عرفی ہے وہ ہے کون الشیئین محسوسین بالبصر والعین، یعنی محسوس بصری و عینی اسی کو عرف میں محسوس کہا جاتا ہے کہ آنکھوں سے مشاہدہ کیا جائے کہ ایک شئی دوسری شئی پر مبنی ہے اور رکھی ہوتی ہے۔ وحينئذ يخرج مثل الخ اس پر بھی اشکال وارد ہو گیا کہ معنی عرفی کے اعتبار سے ابتناء المشتق على المشتق منہ ابتنا حسی سے تو خارج ہو جائے گا لیکن مصنف نے جو ابتناء عقلی کی تعریف و تفسیر کی ہے ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ ابتناء المشتق علی المشتق منہ اس میں بھی داخل نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ مشتق کا ابتنا علی المشتق منہ یہ کوئی ترتب یا ابتنا حکم علی دلیلہ نہیں ہے حالانکہ مشہور یہ ہے کہ ابتناء مشتق علی المشتق منہ ابتاء عقلی میں داخل ہے۔ والحق ان ترتب الحكم على دليله الخ يہاں سے شارح تفتازانی اسی اشکال کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ہم شق ثانی کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں اور محسوس کا معنی عرفی مراد لیتے ہیں اور ابتناء مشتق على المشتق منہ کو بھی اسی ابتناء عقلی میں داخل کرتے ہیں کیونکہ حق بات یہ ہے کہ ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ، ابتغاء عقلی کی تفسیر اور تعریف نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ اس کی چند صورتوں میں سے ایک صورت اور جزئیات میں سے ایک جزئی اور مثال کا ذکر ہے ابتنا عقلی کی تعریف اور ہے وہ ہے ترتب الشئی علی الشئی باعتبار العقل پھر اس کی متعدد جزئیات ہیں مثلا (۱) ترتب المعلولات على العلل (۲) ابتناء المجاز على الحقيقة (۳) ابتناء الاحکام الجزئیة علی الکلیۃ (۴) ابتناء الافعال على المصادر (۵) ابتناء الحكم على دلیلہ تو مصنف نے ترتب الحکم علی دلیلیہ سے ابناء عقلی کی تعریف نہیں ذکر کی بلکہ اس کی جزئیات میں سے ایک جزئی جو کہ یہاں مراد و مقصود تھی اس کو بطور مثال ذکر کر دیا کیونکہ اصول الفقہ میں اصول کا معنی دلیل ہے لہذا ابتناء المشتق على المشتق منہ ابتنا عقلی میں داخل رہے گا۔ سوال ! اگر ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ کو ابتغاء عقلی کی تعریف بنایا جائے تو اس سے کیا قباحت لازم آتی ہے للقطع بان الا بتناء سے شارح اسی شبہ کا ازالہ کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ کو تعریف بنادیا جائے تو ابتنا عقلی کی تعریف جامع نہیں رہے گی ابتناء المجاز علی الحقیقۃ، ابتغاء الافعال على المصادر، ابتناء المعلولات على العلل ، وغیرہ یہ تمام جزئیات ابتنا عقلی سے خارج ہو جائیں گے حالانکہ یہ سب ابتاء عقلی ہیں اسی لیے ہم ترتب الحکم کو تعریف نہیں بناتے بلکہ مثال بناتے ہیں تعریف جامع وہی ہے ترتب الشئی علی الشئى باعتبار العقل (واللہ اعلم بالصواب)۔
If you say: 'Ibnā' is the resting of a thing upon a thing' – the purpose of the commentator Taftazani is an objection and answer. The objection is that the division of ibnā' into sensory and intellectual is false; rather, ibnā' is only intellectual, because ibnā' is the name of the relation between the based and the base, and it is a masdari meaning, an abstract meaning, a relative meaning, and an intellectual meaning which does not exist in the external world, because the masdari meaning is of the category of relation, and the relation as such is non-existent in the external, while sensory ibnā' requires external existence. So it is proven that ibnā' is always intellectual and cannot be sensory; thus dividing ibnā' into sensory and intellectual would be dividing a thing into itself and its other, which is false. The answer: The commentator replies that the division of ibnā' into sensory and intellectual is not with respect to ibnā' itself (which is a relational meaning) but with respect to the two sides, i.e., the based and the base. So sensory ibnā' means the two things being sensory, and intellectual ibnā' means the two things being intellectual. Hence the division is correct. Then [the author] gave two meanings for 'the two things being sensory': (1) they are sensory through any of the five senses, whether eye or ear etc. But under this meaning, just as the resting of the roof on the wall is included in sensory ibnā', so too the derivation of a derivative from its source (the derivation of a verb from a verbal noun) would be included in sensory ibnā', because although it is not visible by sight, it is heard by hearing, like 'sharb' and 'darb' are heard, so it falls under the five senses. Yet the well-known view is that the derivation of a derivative from its source is intellectual. (2) The second meaning of sensory ibnā' is conventional: it is that the two things are sensory by sight and eye, i.e., visually sensory; in convention this is called sensory, that one sees with the eyes that one thing rests upon another and is placed upon it. Then such [verbal derivation] is excluded. But another objection arises: according to the conventional meaning, the derivation of a derivative from its source is excluded from sensory ibnā'; however, the author's definition of intellectual ibnā' as 'the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence' would not include the derivation of a derivative from its source either, because the derivation of a derivative from its source is not an ordering or ibnā' of a ruling upon evidence, yet it is well-known that the derivation of a derivative from its source is included in intellectual ibnā'. The truth is that 'the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence' is not the definition of intellectual ibnā' but is one of its forms and one of its particulars and an example. The definition of intellectual ibnā' is: the resting of a thing upon a thing by consideration of the intellect. Then it has many particulars, e.g., (1) the ordering of effects upon causes, (2) the derivation of metaphor from literal, (3) the ordering of particular rulings upon universal [principles], (4) the derivation of actions from verbal nouns, (5) the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence. So the author did not mention 'the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence' as a definition of intellectual ibnā' but as one of its particulars intended here. Because in uṣūl al-fiqh, 'aṣl' means evidence, so the derivation of a derivative from its source remains included in intellectual ibnā'. Question: If 'the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence' is taken as a definition of intellectual ibnā', what objection follows? The commentator resolves this doubt: if it is taken as a definition, then the definition of intellectual ibnā' would not be comprehensive; the derivation of metaphor from literal, derivation of actions from verbal nouns, ordering of effects upon causes, etc., all these particulars would be excluded from intellectual ibnā', whereas they are all intellectual ibnā'. Therefore we do not make 'ordering of a ruling' a definition but an example. The comprehensive definition is: the resting of a thing upon a thing by consideration of the intellect. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from Sharḥ al-Talwīḥ, where the commentator Taftazani addresses an objection against the division of ibnā' (resting/basing) into sensory and intellectual forms. The objector claims that ibnā' is inherently a relational mental concept, so it cannot be sensory. The response clarifies that the division is based on the two terms (based and base), not the relation itself. Two interpretations of 'sensory' are examined: the first via any sense leads to paradox—verbal derivation would be audible and thus sensory—but the conventional understanding restricts sensory to visual. A second objection is then resolved: the author's phrase 'ordering of ruling upon evidence' is not the definition but an example; intellectual ibnā' is defined as any ordering by intellect, with numerous instances. This is a Hanafi usul discussion, foundational for understanding how rulings rest on evidence and how analogical reasoning (qiyās) works.

Key Terms
ابتناء (ibnā’): The resting or basing of one thing upon another, a relational masdar meaning.
حسی (ḥissī): Pertaining to the senses; here defined conventionally as visually perceptible.
عقلی (ʿaqlī): Intellectual; here defined as the resting of a thing upon a thing by consideration of the intellect.
ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ (tarattub al-ḥukm ʿalā dalīlihi): The ordering of a ruling upon its evidence; one particular instance of intellectual ibnā’.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is the division of ibnā' into sensory and intellectual valid?
A) Because ibnā' itself can be either sensory or intellectual.
B) Because the two sides (based and base) can be sensory or intellectual, not the relation.
C) Because the author defined intellectual ibnā' as ordering of a ruling upon its evidence.
D) Because sensory ibnā' includes audible derivations.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'ordering of a ruling upon its evidence' is an example of intellectual ibnā', not its definition, which is general: the resting of a thing upon a thing by consideration of the intellect.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Ittiraad Dispute: Condition for Definitions in Hanafi Usul
Sharh Taftazani's objection and seven Hanafi responses on the necessity of ittiraad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the usul dispute over ittiraad in definitions and apply the Hanafi position that ta'rif ismi requires ittiraad, distinguishing it from ta'rif lafzi and ta'rif naqis.

Core Idea
Ittiraad is required in technical definitions (ta'rif ismi) but not in lexical or incomplete definitions.

In this passage, the commentator Taftazani challenges the author's rejection of Imam al-Razi's definition of 'asl' on the grounds that it lacks ittiraad. Taftazani argues that ittiraad is not necessary in any definition, especially not in ismi definitions. The author, Sadr al-Shariah, and subsequent Hanafi scholars defend the necessity of ittiraad for precise technical definitions. This lesson examines the core methodological dispute and its implications for defining key usul terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The dispute is about whether ittiraad (comprehensiveness) is a necessary condition for all definitions or just for complete definitions.
Understand the difference between ta'rif tam (complete) and ta'rif naqis (incomplete).
2
State Taftazani's objection and his two proofs
Taftazani argues that ittiraad is not required because lexicons use broader terms, and scholars distinguish complete from incomplete definitions.
The two proofs: (1) lexical definitions with a'amm, (2) division into ta'rif tam and naqis.
3
Analyze the Hanafi responses
The author's defense includes seven responses, notably the distinction between ta'rif lafzi and ta'rif ismi, the role of necessity in lexicon, and the requirement for harmony in defining relative terms.
Focus on response (6) which directly refutes the lexical argument.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if ittiraad is not required, Razi's definition of 'asl' is acceptable; if required, it is rejected.
This affects the entire subsequent usul analysis built on the definition of 'asl'.
5
Apply the Hanafi ruling
For a definition in usul al-fiqh, a complete (mutarid wa mani') definition is preferred; incomplete definitions are only permissible when partial distinction suffices.
The definition of 'asl' in qiyas must be mutarid and mani'.

تو وہ غیر مطرد ہو جاتی ہے کیونکہ لامحالہ اس تعریف میں ایسے افراد داخل ہو جائیں گے جو کہ معرف ومحدود میں داخل نہیں تو جب کتب لغت میں الفاظ کی تعریف وتفسیر الفاظ عامہ کے ساتھ کی گئی ہے اور ہے بھی یہ تعریف امی اور ان کے اوپر کسی نے نقض و اشکال بھی وارد نہیں کیا اور ان کی صحت کو تسلیم کیا ہے تو اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ تعریفات اسمیہ میں طرد شرط نہیں ہے تو آپ کا قاعدہ کلیہ کہ مطلق تعریف میں اطراد شرط ہے باطل ہو گیا دلیل (۲) محققون نے تصریح کی ہے کہ تعریف کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) تعریف ناقص (۲) تعریف تام، تعریف تام میں طرد شرط ہے اور تعریفات ناقصہ میں شرط نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ تعریفات ناقصہ میں جائز ہے کہ ہوتا بلکہ بعض معین اشیاء سے ممتاز کرنا مقصود ہوتا ہے اور تعریف ناقص کی صحت کیلئے یہی بات ( امتیاز عن بعض ما عداه ) ہی کافی ہے مثلا یہاں اصل کو ایک نئی معین (فرع) سے ممتاز کرنا مقصود ہے تو اس کی ایسی تعریف کی جائے گی جو اس کو فرع سے ممتاز کر دے اگر چہ وہ تعریف مانع عن دخول الغیر نہ ہو جیسے علت فاعلیہ صوریہ وغیرہ لہذا ہم اصل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ اور فرع کی محتاج کے ساتھ کرتے ہیں یہ دونوں آپس میں ممتاز ہو جائیں گے اور یہی ہمارا مقصود ہے اگر چہ یہ تعریف مانع اور معطر نہیں ہے محدود کے علاوہ بھی بہت سے افراد پر صادق آرہی ہے لہذا متقین کی تصریح سے ثابت ہوا کہ مطلق تعریف کیلئے طرد و مانع ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ صرف تعریفات تامہ کیلئے ضروری ہے تعریفات ناقصہ کیلئے ضروری نہیں ہے جواب : شارح تفتازانی کے اس اشکال کے متعدد جوابات دیے گئے ہیں۔ جواب ! (۱) آپ کا یہ اشکال آپ ہی کے قول کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ چند سطور قبل آپ ہی کے الفاظ مبارکہ گذر چکے ہیں وهذا الا ظل لہ فی بیان فساد التعریف از عدم الاطراد مفسدله جواب ! (۲) آپ نے خطبہ میں ارشاد فرمایا تھا کہ میں اصول منطق کی رعایت کروں گا اور عند المناطقہ تو اطراد مطلقا ( ہر تعریف میں ) ضروری ہے تو آپ کا یہ قول مناطقہ کے قواعد کے خلاف ہے۔ جواب ! (۳) مصنف نے عدم اطراد والا اعتراض امام رازمی پر وارد کیا ہے اور امام رازی مطلقا ہر تعریف میں طرد اور منع کو شرط قرار دیتے ہیں چنانچہ شرح ارشادات میں امام رازی نے تصریح کردی ہے کہ تعریف با الائم جائز نہیں ہے لہذا اگر یہاں وہ خود تعریف بالائم کریں جو محدود ( اصل ) اور غیر محدود ( علت صور یہ وفاعلیه و غیره) دونوں کو شامل ہو تو یہ مسیح نہیں ہوگا۔ جواب ! (۴) تسلیم ہے کہ اطراد مطلقا تعریف میں شرط نہیں ہے لیکن اولی تو ہے تو مصنف کی کلام درست اور اولیٰ پر محمول ہے۔ جواب ! (۵) یہاں حد اضافی کی بحث ہے جس کے دو جزء ہیں اصول اور فقہ آگے جو فقہ کی تعریف کی جائے گی وہ مطرد ہے لہذا اصول کی تعریف بھی مطرد ہونی چاہیے تا کہ مناسبت حاصل ہوا گرچہ اطراد شرط نہیں ہے لیکن اس مقام میں اطراد ہونا چاہئے تعریف رازی میں چونکہ اطراد نہیں ہے لہذا اس مقام پر وہ درست نہیں ۔ جواب ! (۲) یہ جو شارح تفتازانی نے استدلال فرمایا فان كتب اللغة مشهورة بتفسير الالفاظ بالاهم تو اس کا جواب عرض خدمت ہے کہ حضرت تفتازانی کا یہ استدلال غلط فہمی پرمبنی ہے کیونکہ یہ تمام تعریفات جو کتب لغت میں ہیں ان کو تعریفات لفظیہ کہا جاتا ہے یہ تعریفات اسمیہ نہیں ہیں ان دونوں میں بہت فرق ہے امور بدیعیہ کی تعریف لفظی تو ہو سکتی ہے تعریف اسمی نہیں میں طرد شروا نہیں ہے جب کہ تعریف اسمی میں اور تعریف لفظی میں طرد شرط ہے چونکہ آپ نے تعریف لفظی اور تعریف اسی کوشئی واحد تصور کر لیا ہے اسی غلط فہمی کی بناء پر اصل کی تعریف میں اطراد شرط قرار نہیں دیا حالانکہ اصل کی تعریف اسمی ہے اور اس میں اطراد شرط ہے نیز کتب لغت میں جو تعریف با الاعم کی گئی ہیں وہ بوجہ مجبوری اور اضطرار کے ہیں کیونکہ لفظ مترادف کبھی موجود نہیں ہوتا اسی طرح لفظ اشہر من المعرف بھی نہیں ہوتا تو بحالت اضطرار تعریفات عامہ اختیار کرنی پڑتی ہیں بحالت اضطرار تو میتہ بھی حلال ہو جاتا ہے فمن اضطر غیر باغ ولا عاد فلا اثم عليه - جواب ! (۷) دلیل دوم جو شارح نے فقد صرح سے ذکر کی ہے۔ اولا تو سعد کا فقد صرح المحققون کہنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ محققون کا مذہب نہیں ہے بلکہ مذہب بعض ہے نیز اس دلیل سے مصنف پر کوئی اشکال وارد نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اس میں خود شارح تسلیم کر رہے ہیں کہ جو تعریفات بالا ئم ہوتی ہیں وہ ناقص ہوتی ہیں لہذا احتاج الیہ کے ساتھ تعریف ناقص ہوگی جو مانع عن دخول الغیر نہیں ہوگی جو امتیاز عن جمیع ما عداہ کا فائدہ نہیں دے گی پس یہی تو وہ وجوہات ہیں جن کی بناء پر مصنف نے اس تعریف کو قابل اعتراض سمجھ کر ترک کر دیا ہے اور تعریف کامل کو اختیار کیا ہے
And here is a discussion from several aspects. From here, Sharh Taftazani is raising several objections against the author. The first: the summary of the first objection is that you (author) declared Imam al-Razi's definition invalid because it is not comprehensive (mutarid) and not preventive (mani'). The basis of your objection is that in absolute definition (i.e., every type of definition), ittiraad (comprehensiveness) is a condition, whether the definition is haqiqi or ismi. We do not accept your statement; rather, our claim is that in absolute definition, ittiraad is not necessary, especially in ismi definitions it is absolutely not necessary. So if Imam al-Razi's definition is not mutarid, there is no problem. The commentator presents two proofs that ittiraad is not a condition in ismi definitions: (1) The first proof from lexicons: in lexicons there are many words whose definition and explanation is given with words that are more general than the defined term, e.g., 'al-sa'd' being defined as 'nabt', 'al-dhi'b' as 'sabu'', etc. When a definition is more general than the defined, it becomes non-mutarid because inevitably it includes individuals not included in the defined. Since lexicons define words with general words, and this is ismi definition, and no one has objected to their validity, this proves that in ismi definitions ittiraad is not a condition, thus your universal rule that ittiraad is a condition in absolute definition is false. (2) The verifiers have stated that there are two types of definition: (a) ta'rif naqis (incomplete definition) and (b) ta'rif tam (complete definition). In ta'rif tam, ittiraad is a condition; in ta'rif naqis, it is not. That is why in ta'rif naqis, it is permissible that it be more general than the defined; then such definitions will not be comprehensive (mani' 'an dukhul al-ghair). The benefit of ta'rif naqis is that sometimes the purpose is not to distinguish the defined from all other things, but only from some specific things. For correctness of ta'rif naqis, this distinction from some others suffices. For example, here we intend to distinguish 'asl' from a specific 'far''; so we define it in a way that distinguishes it from far', even if it is not preventive of entry of other things, like cause (fā'ilī, sūrī, etc.). Therefore, we define 'asl' as 'what is in need' and 'far'' as 'that which is in need'. They are distinguished from each other, and that is our purpose, although this definition is not preventive or mutarid and applies to many other individuals besides the defined. So from the statement of the verifiers, it is established that ittiraad and man' are not necessary for absolute definition, but only for complete definitions; they are not necessary for incomplete definitions. Responses: Several responses have been given to this objection of Sharh Taftazani. Response (1): Your objection contradicts your own statement because a few lines ago your own words passed: 'and this is the most apparent for him in explaining the invalidity of the definition due to lack of ittiraad corrupts it.' Response (2): You stated in the preface that you will observe the principles of logic, and for logicians, ittiraad is necessary absolutely (in every definition), so your statement here opposes the rules of logic. Response (3): The author raised the objection of lack of ittiraad against Imam al-Razi, and Imam al-Razi absolutely makes ittiraad and man' a condition in every definition; thus in Sharh al-Irshadat, Imam al-Razi stated clearly that definition by more general is not permissible. So if here he himself gives a definition by more general that includes both the defined (asl) and other things (sūrī cause, fā'ilī cause, etc.), that would not be sound. Response (4): It is conceded that ittiraad is not a condition in absolute definition, but it is preferable; so the author's words are correct and carry the preferable meaning. Response (5): Here we are discussing al-hadd al-idāfī (relative definition), which has two parts: usul and fiqh. The definition of fiqh that will come later is mutarid; so the definition of usul should also be mutarid for harmony. Even if ittiraad is not a condition, in this place ittiraad is required. Razi's definition lacks ittiraad, so it is not correct in this context. Response (6): Regarding Taftazani's argument that lexicons are well-known for interpreting words with more general, the response is that this argument is based on misunderstanding, because all these definitions in lexicons are called 'ta'rif lafzi' (lexical definitions); they are not 'ta'rif ismi' (technical definitions). There is a great difference between them. In ta'rif lafzi, ittiraad is not a condition, while in ta'rif ismi it is a condition. Since you assumed ta'rif lafzi and ta'rif ismi to be the same, you did not consider ittiraad a condition in the definition of 'asl', whereas the definition of 'asl' is ismi and requires ittiraad. Moreover, the definitions in lexicons made with more general are due to constraint and necessity, because sometimes no synonymous word exists or there is no word more famous than the defined. In necessity, general definitions are adopted; in necessity, even carrion becomes lawful: 'But if one is forced by necessity, without willful disobedience or transgression, then no sin upon him.' Response (7): Regarding the second proof that the commentator mentioned from 'the verifiers stated' – firstly, the phrase 'the verifiers stated' is not correct because this is not the view of all verifiers but of some. Also, this argument does not cause objection against the author, because the commentator himself concedes that definitions that are more general are incomplete. Therefore, defining 'asl' with 'muhāj' (in need) is an incomplete definition that does not prevent entry of other things and does not give distinction from all others. These are precisely the reasons why the author considered this definition objectionable and left it, and adopted the complete definition.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection of the commentator (Taftazani) against the author (Sadr al-Shariah) regarding the definition of 'asl' (origin). The author had rejected Imam al-Razi's definition because it lacked ittiraad (comprehensiveness) and man' (preventiveness). Taftazani argues that ittiraad is not required in all definitions, especially in ismi (technical) definitions, and he provides two proofs: first, lexicons use broader terms, and second, there is a distinction between complete and incomplete definitions. The passage then lists seven responses in defense of the author, each refuting Taftazani's points. The key usul principle debated is whether ittiraad is a necessary condition for definitions in usul al-fiqh. The Hanafi position, as represented by the author, is that in definitions of technical terms (ta'rif ismi), ittiraad is indeed required, otherwise the definition fails to be exhaustive and exclusive. The commentator's reliance on lexical definitions is refuted by distinguishing ta'rif lafzi (linguistic) from ta'rif ismi, and by noting that lexical definitions are often forced by necessity. The final response (7) points out that the commentator's second proof is not from a consensus of verifiers but only some, and that the incomplete definition is precisely why the author avoids it. This shows the rigorous methodological standards in Hanafi usul for defining key terms.

Key Terms
اطراد (itṭirād): Comprehensiveness of a definition; that it applies to all individuals of the defined term.
تعریف ناقص (ta'rīf nāqiṣ): An incomplete definition that does not distinguish the defined from all other things but only from some.
تعریف تام (ta'rīf tāmm): A complete definition that distinguishes the defined from everything else (mutarid wa mani').
تعریف اسمی (ta'rīf ismī): A definition of a term by mentioning its essence or distinguishing properties, often requiring precision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the responses defending the author, why does the definition of 'asl' as 'muhāj ilayh' fail?
A) It is not found in the lexicons.
B) It is a complete definition but rejected by Imam Razi.
C) It is an incomplete definition (ta'rif naqis) that does not prevent entry of non-‘asl elements.
D) It is too general and includes all causes.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, complete technical definitions (ta'rif tam) require ittiraad and man', whereas incomplete definitions (ta'rif naqis) may suffice when only partial distinction is needed.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Requirement of Universality in Defining 'al-Asl'
Analyzing objections to Imam al-Razi's definition of al-asl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid nominal definition and evaluate why Imam al-Razi's definition of 'al-asl' as 'al-muhtaj ilayh' fails to meet them.

Core Idea
A nominal definition must be universal (mutṭarid) and exclusive (māniʻ); 'al-muhtaj ilayh' fails because it covers causes beyond the material.

In usul al-fiqh, precise definitions are critical to avoid confusion in legal reasoning. This passage examines a key dispute about the definition of 'al-asl' (the origin/source), the foundational term in analogical deduction. By analyzing the objections to Imam al-Razi's broad definition, we uncover why Hanafis insist that a nominal definition must be universally applicable to all instances and exclusive to them. Let's step through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Term and the Dispute
First, recognize that 'al-asl' is a central term in usul al-fiqh. The passage contrasts Imam al-Razi's definition ('that which is needed', al-muhtaj ilayh) with the Hanafi view that it refers only to the material cause (al-illa al-maddiyya).
The material cause is the substrate upon which something is built, e.g., wood for a chair.
2
Recall the Condition of Ittirād
A nominal definition (ta'rīf ismī) must be mutṭarid: it must apply to every instance of the definiendum and only to those instances. This principle comes from logic and is accepted by Hanafi usulis for technical definitions.
Verbal definitions (found in lexicons) are looser; they may use a broader term due to necessity.
3
Apply Ittirād to al-Razi's Definition
Test the definition 'al-muhtaj ilayh' against the condition. It applies not only to the material cause but also to the efficient, formal, final, and conditional causes. Since 'asl' in actual Arabic usage is restricted to the material cause, the definition fails universality.
The efficient cause is the agent, the formal cause is the form, the final cause is the purpose, and the condition is a prerequisite.
4
Analyze the Counterarguments
The passage addresses several objections: (i) that the definition might apply to the efficient cause, (ii) that the author contradicts himself in the chapter on majaz, and (iii) that the definition could be rescued by considering it a verbal definition. The commentator refutes each, reinforcing the need for universality.
For the efficient cause objection, the response is that 'ibnā' means foundational attribution, not efficient causation.
5
Conclude the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi position is that a valid definition of 'asl' must be mutṭarid and restricted to the material cause. A definition like 'al-muhtaj ilayh' is acceptable only in specific contexts (e.g., distinguishing haqiqa from majaz) but not as a general technical definition.
This precision safeguards the integrity of istinbāt (derivation) by ensuring that analogies are built on the correct foundation.

اسمیا کان اوغیرہ۔ ان دونوں کو دیکھ لیجئے اور پھر فیصلہ کیجئے کہ علامہ صدر پر آپ کا یہ اعتراض صحیح ہے یا غلط۔ جواب ! (۷) دلیل دوم جو شارح نے فقد صرح سے ذکر کی ہے۔ اولا تو سعد کا فقد صرح المحققون کہنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ محققون کا مذہب نہیں ہے بلکہ مذہب بعض ہے نیز اس دلیل سے مصنف پر کوئی اشکال وارد نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اس میں خود شارح تسلیم کر رہے ہیں کہ جو تعریفات بالا ئم ہوتی ہیں وہ ناقص ہوتی ہیں لہذا احتاج الیہ کے ساتھ تعریف ناقص ہوگی جو مانع عن دخول الغیر نہیں ہوگی جو امتیاز عن جمیع ما عداہ کا فائدہ نہیں دے گی پس یہی تو وہ وجوہات ہیں جن کی بناء پر مصنف نے اس تعریف کو قابل اعتراض سمجھ کر ترک کر دیا ہے اور تعریف کامل کو اختیار کیا ہے الثانى منع عدم صدق الاصل اشکال ثانی یہ ہے کہ مصنف کا یہ قول کہ اصل کا اطلاق صرف علت مادی پر ہوتا ہے علت فاعلی پر نہیں ہوتا اس کو ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے بلکہ اس کا اطلاق علت فاعلی پر ہوسکتا ہے کیونکہ اصل کی تعریف تھی یا جتنی علیہ غیرہ
مسک الملیح یہ تعریف علت فاعلی پر بھی صادق آتی ہے کیونکہ وجود فعل مترتب وپینی علی الفاعل ہوتا ہے اور فعل کا استنادالی الفاعل ہوتا ہے اور اصل کی تعریف میں ابتاء علی الخیر سے مراد بھی یہی ہے کہ اس شئی کا استناد اور ترتب ہو غیر پر الہذا اصل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ جس طرح فاعل پر صادق آتی ہے اسی طرح معرف ومحدود (الاصل ) بھی فائل پر صادق آتا ہے تو عدم اطراد والا اشکال غلط ہو گا جواب اس اشکال کے متعدد جوابات ہیں۔ جواب ! (۱) اول یہ ہے کہ تسلیم ہے کہ اصل کی تعریف فاعل پر سچی آتی ہے اور اصل کا اطلاق فاعل پر ہو سکتا ہے لیکن مصنف کی مراد یہ ہے کہ لفظ اصل کا اطلاق یا الفعل صرف علت مادی پر ہوتا ہے اور اس کا اطلاق اور استعمال بالفعل فاعل پر واقع نہیں ہے فی کلام العرب اگر کلام عرب میں اطلاق علی الفاعل ثابت ہو جائے تو پھر مصنف پر اشکال وارد ہو سکتا ہے لیکن یہ قل پیش نہیں کی جاسکتی (۲) اگر بالفرض تسلیم کر لیا جائے کہ اطلاق اصل علی الفاعل ثابت ہے تب بھی اشکال مصنف علی تعریف الرازی (بانه غیر مطرد ) برقرار رہے گا کیونکہ علت صوریہ غائیہ اور شرط پر اصل کا اطلاق پھر بھی نہیں ہوتا اور تعریف محتاج الیہ صادق آتی ہے تو تعریف پھر بھی غیر مطر د ہے۔ (۳) اصل کا اطلاق علی الفاعل نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ ابتغاء سے مراد استناد اساسی ہے نہ کہ استناد تا ثیری یعنی ابتناء انشئی علی الخیر سے مراد یہ ہے کہ یہ غیر اس شئی کیلئے بمنزلہ اساس کے ہونہ یہ کہ وہ غیر اس شئی کے وجود میں مؤثر ہو فاعل مؤثر فی وجود الفعل ہوتا ہے ایسا نہیں کہ فاعل ایک اساس ہو اور اس پر فعل کی بناء ہو لہذا ما یقینی علیہ غیرہ والی تعریف فاعل پر صادق نہیں ہو سکتی الثالث ان كلامه فى باب المجاز الخ تیسرا اشکال یہ ہے کہ مصنف کی عبارت میں تعارض ہے کیونکہ یہاں مصنف نے یہ فرمایا ہرمحتاج الیہ پر اصل کا طلاق نہیں ہوتا آگے چل کر باب المجاز میں جریان الاصالۃ والتبعیۃ من الجانبین میں جو کلام کی ہے وہ دلالت کرتی ہے کہ ہر محتاج الیہ اصل ہے تو جب مصنف باب المجاز میں ہر محتاج الیہ کا اصل ہونا تسلیم کر رہا ہے تو پھر امام رازی نے الاصل کی جو تعریف المحتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کی ہے یہ کل اعتراض کیوں ہے اس پر مصنف کیوں اشکال وارد کر رہے ہیں۔ جواب ! مصنف کی عبارت جو باب المجاز میں ہے وہ قطعا اس پر دال نہیں ہے کہ ہر محتاج الیہ اصل کہلاتا ہے بلکہ مراد مصنف یہ ہے کہ جب حقیقت جو بدرجہ اصل ہے اور مجاز جو بدرجہ فرع ہے ان دونوں کے درمیان اشتباہ پیدا ہو جائے اور ان کے درمیان امتیاز کرنا ہو تو دیکھا جائے گا کہ ان میں سے محتاج الیہ اور محتاج کون ہے جو محتاج الیہ ہو گا اس کو اصل (حقیقت) اور جو محتاج ہو گا اس کو فرع ( مجاز ) کہا جائے گا تو اس سے تو ایک خاص مقام کے اعتبار سے محتاج الیہ اصل قرار دیا گیا ہے تا کہ حقیقت اور مجاز کے درمیان امتیاز ہو جائے تو ایک خاص مقام پر اصل کی تفسیر محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کرنا اس کو تلزم نہیں ہے کہ مطلقا ہر اصل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کرنا صحیح ہو۔ الرابع انا اذا قلنا الخ صنف پر چوتھا اشکال ہے کہ اگر امام رازی کی تعریف مطرد مانع نہیں ہے تو آپ کی تعریف الاصل منعکس و جامع نہیں ہے مثلاً جب فکر کی تعریف کی جائے یوں کہا جائے الفکر ترتیب امور معلومہ تو امور معلومہ فکر کیلئے علت مادی اور اصل ہیں ترتیب امور
If the definition is by a broader term, etc. Look at these two and decide whether your objection against 'Allama Sadr is correct or wrong. Answer (2): You stated in the sermon that I will observe the principles of logic, and according to logicians, universality (itrad) is absolutely necessary in every definition, so your statement is against the rules of logicians. Answer (3): The author raised the objection of lack of universality against Imam al-Razi, and Imam al-Razi absolutely makes universality and exclusivity conditions in every definition, as clarified in Sharh al-Irshadat that definition by a broader term is not permissible. So if here he himself defines by a broader term that includes both the defined (asl) and the non-defined (formal cause, efficient cause, etc.), then it will not be correct. Answer (4): We accept that universality is not absolutely a condition in definition, but it is preferable, so the author's statement is correct and interpreted as preferable. Answer (5): Here the discussion is about relative definition, which has two parts: usul and fiqh. Later the definition of fiqh will be universal, so the definition of usul should also be universal to achieve suitability. Even if universality is not a condition, in this context universality is required; since al-Razi's definition lacks universality, it is not correct here. Answer (2): As for the argument of Sharh Taftazani that 'lexical books are famous for interpreting words by the more common meaning', the reply is that this argument of Taftazani is based on misunderstanding because all these definitions in lexical books are called verbal definitions (ta'rifat lafziyya), not nominal definitions (ta'rifat ismiyya). There is a great difference between them. The definition of intellectual matters can be verbal, not nominal, and universality is not a condition in verbal definitions, while in nominal definitions universality is a condition. Since you considered verbal and nominal definitions as one thing, you did not make universality a condition in the definition of 'asl', whereas the definition of 'asl' is nominal and universality is a condition in it. Also, the definitions by a broader term in lexical books are due to necessity and compulsion, because a synonym is never available, nor a term more well-known than the defined term. So in necessity, general definitions have to be adopted; in necessity, even carrion becomes permissible: 'But if one is forced by necessity, neither desiring nor transgressing, there is no sin upon him.' Answer (7): As for the second proof that the commentator mentioned from 'they explicitly stated', firstly, Sa'd's saying 'the investigators explicitly stated' is not correct because this is not the view of all investigators but only of some. Also, this proof does not pose any objection against the author, because in it the commentator himself admits that definitions by a broader term are deficient. So the definition with 'al-muhtaj ilayh' will be deficient, which will not prevent entry of what is not intended, and will not provide distinction from all others. So these are the reasons why the author considered this definition objectionable and abandoned it, adopting the complete definition. Second: Objection of non-applicability of 'asl'. The second objection is that the author's statement that the term 'asl' applies only to the material cause (illa maddiyya) and not to the efficient cause (illa fa'iliyya) is not accepted; rather, it can apply to the efficient cause because the definition of 'asl' is 'that upon which something else is based'. This definition also applies to the efficient cause because existence of the act is arranged upon the agent, and the act is attributed to the agent. And in the definition of 'asl', 'ibna' upon the other means the attribution and arrangement of that thing upon the other. So the definition of 'asl' as 'al-muhtaj ilayh' applies to the agent just as it applies to the material cause, and thus the limited (al-asl) also applies to the agent. So the objection of lack of universality is false. There are several answers to this objection. Answer (1): First, we accept that the definition of 'asl' applies to the agent and the term 'asl' can be applied to the agent, but the author's intent is that the term 'asl' in actual usage applies only to the material cause, and its actual application and use for the agent does not occur in the speech of the Arabs. If application to the agent were proven in Arabic speech, then the objection against the author could be raised, but this cannot be easily claimed. (2) Even if, hypothetically, we accept that the application of 'asl' to the agent is proven, the author's objection against al-Razi's definition (that it is not universal) would still stand, because application of 'asl' to the formal cause, final cause, and condition still does not occur, while the definition 'al-muhtaj ilayh' applies to them, so the definition is still not universal. (3) The term 'asl' cannot be applied to the agent because 'ibna' means foundational attribution, not efficient attribution; i.e., 'ibna' in the sense of being like a foundation for the other, not that it is effective in the existence of the other. The agent is effective in the existence of the act, not such that the agent is a foundation and the act is built upon it. Therefore, the definition 'ma yabna 'alayhi ghayruhu' does not apply to the agent. Third: That his statement in the chapter of majaz, etc. The third objection is that there is contradiction in the author's statement because here the author said 'the term 'asl' does not apply to everything that is needed' (muhtaj ilayh). Later, in the chapter of majaz, his statement about the flow of originality and subordination from both sides indicates that everything that is needed is 'asl'. So if the author in the chapter of majaz accepts that everything needed is 'asl', then why does he object to Imam al-Razi's definition of 'asl' as 'al-muhtaj ilayh'? Answer: The author's statement in the chapter of majaz does not at all indicate that everything needed is called 'asl'. Rather, the author's intent is that when reality (haqiqa) which is at the level of 'asl' and metaphor (majaz) which is at the level of branch (far') become ambiguous between them, and one needs to distinguish between them, it will be seen which of them is the needed (muhtaj ilayh) and which is the needing (muhtaj). That which is needed will be called 'asl (haqiqa) and that which is needing will be called far' (majaz). So this confers the name 'asl' on the needed from a specific perspective in order to distinguish between reality and metaphor. Thus, interpreting 'asl' as 'al-muhtaj ilayh' in a specific context does not necessitate that it is correct to define every 'asl' absolutely as 'al-muhtaj ilayh'. Fourth: That if we say, etc. The fourth objection against the author is that if Imam al-Razi's definition is not universal and exclusive, then your definition of 'asl' is not convertible and inclusive. For example, when defining thought (fikr) as 'arrangement of known matters', the known matters are the material cause and 'asl' for thought, and arrangement... (cut off)
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of the term 'al-asl' (the origin/source) in usul al-fiqh, specifically responding to objections raised by Sharh Taftazani against the author's criticism of Imam al-Razi's definition. The central issue is whether a definition must be muttarid (universally applicable to all instances of the definiendum). The commentator explains that Imam al-Razi's definition of 'asl' as 'al-muhtaj ilayh' (that which is needed/relied upon) is problematic because it is not universal: it includes efficient, formal, final, and conditional causes in addition to the material cause, but the term 'asl' in actual Arabic usage (and in usul) is restricted to the material cause. The commentator distinguishes between nominal definitions (ta'rif ismi) and verbal definitions (ta'rif lafzi): universality is a condition in nominal definitions, while verbal definitions (as found in lexicons) may use a broader term due to necessity. The passage then addresses multiple answers to the objection that the definition might apply to the efficient cause, including that the term 'asl' is not actually used for the efficient cause in Arabic, that even if it were, it still wouldn't cover other causes, and that the relationship with the efficient cause is causal, not foundational. Finally, a third objection about an apparent contradiction with the author's later discussion of majaz is resolved by explaining that the term 'asl' is used in a specific context for distinguishing haqiqa from majaz, not universally.

Key Terms
اطراد (iṭṭirād): Universal applicability of a definition to all instances of the definiendum; a condition for a valid nominal definition.
تعریف اسمی (taʿrīf ismī): A nominal definition that defines a term by specifying its essence or real meaning; requires universality and exclusivity.
علت مادی (ʿilla māddiyya): The material cause; the substrate or matter upon which something is built (e.g., wood for a chair). In usul, it is the source from which rulings are derived.
علت فاعلی (ʿilla fāʿiliyya): The efficient cause; the agent that brings something into existence. The text argues it is not called 'asl' in Arabic.
محتاج الیہ (muḥtāj ilayh): That which is needed or relied upon; the definition proposed by Imam al-Razi for 'asl'. The text argues it is too broad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Imam al-Razi's definition of 'al-asl' as 'al-muhtaj ilayh' fail to be a valid nominal definition?
A) It is not derived from the Quran or Sunnah.
B) It is not universal because it applies to the efficient, formal, final, and conditional causes in addition to the material cause.
C) It is a verbal definition, not a nominal definition.
D) It contradicts the author's own definition in the chapter on majaz.

Key Takeaway
A proper nominal definition in usul al-fiqh must be universal (mutṭarid); otherwise, it fails to accurately define the term and can lead to errors in istinbāt.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
10 min
Definition of al-Asl in Hanafi Usul: Refuting Imam al-Razi's View
Critiquing Imam al-Razi's definition of al-Asl and defending the author's definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi definition of al-asl and identify why al-Razi's definition (al-muhtāj ilayh) is rejected as non-universal.

Core Idea
Al-asl is the foundation upon which something is built, not merely a necessary condition.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the term 'asl' is foundational for qiyas and textual interpretation. The passage defends the author's definition — 'that upon which another thing is built' — against Imam al-Razi's equation of asl with 'that which is needed' (muhtāj ilayh). Understanding this distinction is critical for correctly identifying the original case (asl) in analogical reasoning and for distinguishing reality from metaphor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested definitions
Contrast the author's definition (ma yubtānā 'alayhi ghayruh) with al-Razi's (al-muhtāj ilayh). Note that the author's definition emphasizes foundational building, while al-Razi's focuses on necessity.
The difference is subtle but has significant implications for the scope of the term asl.
2
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal of the first objection
Examine why the author's definition is not invalidated by its apparent application to the efficient cause. The commentator explains that 'asl' in Arabic usage is not applied to the agent (fā'il) and that the term 'ibnā'' means foundational attribution, not causal efficacy.
This preserves the definition's exclusivity to material cause and other proper foundations.
3
Resolve the apparent contradiction from the chapter on metaphor
Understand how the author's later statement that 'everything needed is asl' in the context of distinguishing reality from metaphor does not contradict his rejection of al-Razi's absolute definition. The context is specific, not universal.
This shows the importance of contextual interpretation in usul.
4
Evaluate Taftazani's objection and the commentator's response
Taftazani argues that the author's definition of intellectual ibnā' as 'tartīb al-ḥukm 'alā dalīlih' fails to include the instance of thought (fikr) built upon known matters. The commentator counters that Taftazani himself admitted that phrase is merely an example, and the true definition ('tartīb al-shay' 'alā shay' fī al-'aql') does cover thought.
This strengthens the author's definition and exposes inconsistency in Taftazani's criticism.
5
Synthesize the correct Hanafi definition
Consolidate: al-asl is that upon which another thing is built, either sensibly or intellectually. It is not synonymous with muhtāj ilayh. The asl must be a foundational basis, not merely a necessary condition.
This definition is comprehensive (jāmi') and exclusive (māni') for Hanafi usul.

مسک الملیح یہ تعریف علت فاعلی پر بھی صادق آتی ہے کیونکہ وجود فعل مترتب وپینی علی الفاعل ہوتا ہے اور فعل کا استنادالی الفاعل ہوتا ہے اور اصل کی تعریف میں ابتاء علی الخیر سے مراد بھی یہی ہے کہ اس شئی کا استناد اور ترتب ہو غیر پر الہذا اصل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ جس طرح فاعل پر صادق آتی ہے اسی طرح معرف ومحدود (الاصل ) بھی فائل پر صادق آتا ہے تو عدم اطراد والا اشکال غلط ہو گا جواب اس اشکال کے متعدد جوابات ہیں۔ جواب ! (۱) اول یہ ہے کہ تسلیم ہے کہ اصل کی تعریف فاعل پر سچی آتی ہے اور اصل کا اطلاق فاعل پر ہو سکتا ہے لیکن مصنف کی مراد یہ ہے کہ لفظ اصل کا اطلاق یا الفعل صرف علت مادی پر ہوتا ہے اور اس کا اطلاق اور استعمال بالفعل فاعل پر واقع نہیں ہے فی کلام العرب اگر کلام عرب میں اطلاق علی الفاعل ثابت ہو جائے تو پھر مصنف پر اشکال وارد ہو سکتا ہے لیکن یہ قل پیش نہیں کی جاسکتی (۲) اگر بالفرض تسلیم کر لیا جائے کہ اطلاق اصل علی الفاعل ثابت ہے تب بھی اشکال مصنف علی تعریف الرازی (بانه غیر مطرد ) برقرار رہے گا کیونکہ علت صوریہ غائیہ اور شرط پر اصل کا اطلاق پھر بھی نہیں ہوتا اور تعریف محتاج الیہ صادق آتی ہے تو تعریف پھر بھی غیر مطر د ہے۔ (۳) اصل کا اطلاق علی الفاعل نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ ابتغاء سے مراد استناد اساسی ہے نہ کہ استناد تا ثیری یعنی ابتناء انشئی علی الخیر سے مراد یہ ہے کہ یہ غیر اس شئی کیلئے بمنزلہ اساس کے ہونہ یہ کہ وہ غیر اس شئی کے وجود میں مؤثر ہو فاعل مؤثر فی وجود الفعل ہوتا ہے ایسا نہیں کہ فاعل ایک اساس ہو اور اس پر فعل کی بناء ہو لہذا ما یقینی علیہ غیرہ والی تعریف فاعل پر صادق نہیں ہو سکتی الثالث ان كلامه فى باب المجاز الخ تیسرا اشکال یہ ہے کہ مصنف کی عبارت میں تعارض ہے کیونکہ یہاں مصنف نے یہ فرمایا ہرمحتاج الیہ پر اصل کا طلاق نہیں ہوتا آگے چل کر باب المجاز میں جریان الاصالۃ والتبعیۃ من الجانبین میں جو کلام کی ہے وہ دلالت کرتی ہے کہ ہر محتاج الیہ اصل ہے تو جب مصنف باب المجاز میں ہر محتاج الیہ کا اصل ہونا تسلیم کر رہا ہے تو پھر امام رازی نے الاصل کی جو تعریف المحتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کی ہے یہ کل اعتراض کیوں ہے اس پر مصنف کیوں اشکال وارد کر رہے ہیں۔ جواب ! مصنف کی عبارت جو باب المجاز میں ہے وہ قطعا اس پر دال نہیں ہے کہ ہر محتاج الیہ اصل کہلاتا ہے بلکہ مراد مصنف یہ ہے کہ جب حقیقت جو بدرجہ اصل ہے اور مجاز جو بدرجہ فرع ہے ان دونوں کے درمیان اشتباہ پیدا ہو جائے اور ان کے درمیان امتیاز کرنا ہو تو دیکھا جائے گا کہ ان میں سے محتاج الیہ اور محتاج کون ہے جو محتاج الیہ ہو گا اس کو اصل (حقیقت) اور جو محتاج ہو گا اس کو فرع ( مجاز ) کہا جائے گا تو اس سے تو ایک خاص مقام کے اعتبار سے محتاج الیہ اصل قرار دیا گیا ہے تا کہ حقیقت اور مجاز کے درمیان امتیاز ہو جائے تو ایک خاص مقام پر اصل کی تفسیر محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کرنا اس کو تلزم نہیں ہے کہ مطلقا ہر اصل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کرنا صحیح ہو۔ الرابع انا اذا قلنا الخ صنف پر چوتھا اشکال ہے کہ اگر امام رازی کی تعریف مطرد مانع نہیں ہے تو آپ کی تعریف الاصل منعکس و جامع نہیں ہے مثلاً جب فکر کی تعریف کی جائے یوں کہا جائے الفکر ترتیب امور معلومہ تو امور معلومہ فکر کیلئے علت مادی اور اصل ہیں ترتیب امور معلومہ علت صور یہ مفکر علت فاعلیہ اور ایصال الی المحمول علت غائیہ ہے جب امور معلومہ مادہ اور اصل ہیں تو فکر کا ان پر ابتناء ہوگا لیکن ابتناء کی دونوں قسموں میں سے کوئی قسم نہیں بن سکتی فکر کا ابتناء امور معلومہ پر نہ تو حسی ہے دھو ظا ہر اور نہ ابتناء عقلی ہے ، جفسیر المصنف کیونکہ مصنف نے ابتاء عقلی کی تعریف کی ہے ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ اور فکر کا ابتناء علی امور معلومہ یہ ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ فکر حکم نہیں ہے اور امور معلومہ اس کیلئے دلیل نہیں ہے لہذا آپ کی تعریف جامع نہیں ہے۔ جواب ! شارح تفتازانی کا یہ اشکال لغو اور بے سود ہے دراصل تفتازانی نے یہ تہیہ کر رکھا ہے کہ مصنف کی ہر بات کی تردید کرنی ہے اس لیے وہ ہر جائز و نا جائز اشکال کرتا ہے اور یہ بھی نہیں سوچتا کہ یہ میری اپنی کلام کے خلاف ہے . اشکال مذکور بھی اسی کا ایک نمونہ ہے شارح تفتازانی ماقبل میں کہ چکے ہیں۔ والحق ان ترتب الحكم على دليله لاتصلح تغير اللابناء العقلى وانما ھومثال لہ، خود اعتراف کر چکے ہیں کہ ترتب احکم ابتنا عقلی کی تفسیر و تعریف نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ اس کی مثال ہے ابتنا عقلی کی تعریف اور ہے، ترتب الشئی علی شئی فی العقل اور یہ تعریف ترتب الفکر علی امور معلومہ پر بالکل صادق آرہی ہے لہذا تعریف مصنف جامع و منعکس ہے اور اعتراض شارح لغو ہے۔
Misk al-Malih: This definition also applies to the efficient cause, because the existence of the act is sequential and dependent upon the agent, and the act is attributed to the agent. And in the definition of al-asl, 'ibnā' 'alā al-ghayr' means that the thing is attributed to and sequential upon another. Therefore, the definition of al-asl (muhtāj ilayh) just as it applies to the agent, similarly the defined term (al-asl) applies to the agent, so the objection of non-universality is incorrect. The answer to this objection has multiple answers. Answer (1): First, it is conceded that the definition of al-asl applies truly to the agent, and the term al-asl can be applied to the agent, but the author means that the application of the word al-asl specifically to the material cause, and its application and usage to the agent actually does not occur in the Arabic language. If application to the agent were established in Arabic speech, then the objection could be made against the author, but this cannot be claimed. (2) If, by assumption, it is conceded that the application of al-asl to the agent is established, even then the author's objection to al-Razi's definition (that it is not universal) remains, because al-asl is not applied to the formal cause, final cause, and condition, and the definition (muhtāj ilayh) applies to them, so the definition is still not universal. (3) The application of al-asl to the agent is not possible because 'ibnā' means foundational attribution, not effective attribution; i.e., 'binā' inshā'ī 'alā al-ghayr' means that the thing is like a foundation for the other, not that it is effective in the existence of the other. The agent is effective in the existence of the act, not that the agent is a foundation upon which the act is built. Therefore, the definition 'mā yubtānā 'alayhi ghayruh' does not apply to the agent. Third: His statement in the chapter on metaphor... The third objection is that there is a contradiction in the author's words because here the author says that al-asl is not applied to everything needed, but later in the chapter on metaphor regarding the flow of originality and subordinateness from both sides, his speech indicates that everything needed is al-asl. So when the author acknowledges in the chapter on metaphor that everything needed is al-asl, then why does he object to Imam al-Razi's definition of al-asl as 'al-muhtāj ilayh'? Answer: The author's words in the chapter on metaphor do not absolutely indicate that everything needed is called al-asl; rather, the author means that when the reality (which is on the level of asl) and the metaphor (which is on the level of far') become confused and need to be distinguished, it will be seen which of them is muhtāj ilayh and which is muhtāj. That which is muhtāj ilayh will be called asl (reality) and that which is muhtāj will be called far' (metaphor). So this is considering a particular context to make the asl muhtāj ilayh in order to distinguish reality and metaphor. Defining al-asl as muhtāj ilayh in a particular context does not necessitate that it is correct to define every asl as muhtāj ilayh absolutely. Fourth: If we say... The fourth objection against the author is that if Imam al-Razi's definition is not universal and exclusive, then your definition of al-asl is not converse and comprehensive. For example, when defining thought, it is said: 'al-fikr tartīb al-umūr al-ma'lūmah' (thought is the arrangement of known matters). Then the known matters are the material cause and the asl for thought. The arrangement of known matters is the formal cause, the thinker is the efficient cause, and reaching the conclusion is the final cause. When the known matters are the matter and the asl, then thought has an ibnā' upon them, but it cannot be either of the two types of ibnā'. The ibnā' of thought upon known matters is neither sensory (evident) nor intellectual, because the author defined intellectual ibnā' as 'tartīb al-ḥukm 'alā dalīlih' (the order of a ruling upon its evidence). The ibnā' of thought upon known matters is not this, because thought is not a ruling and the known matters are not evidence for it. Therefore, your definition is not comprehensive. Answer: This objection of Sharīḥ Taftāzānī is frivolous and useless. In fact, Taftāzānī has resolved to refute every statement of the author, so he raises every objection, valid or invalid, and does not consider that it contradicts his own statement. This objection is also an example of this. Sharīḥ Taftāzānī has previously said: 'Wa al-ḥaqq anna tartīb al-ḥukm 'alā dalīlih lā taṣluḥ tafsīran li'l-ibnā' al-'aqlī wa innamā huwa mithālun lahu' (And the truth is that the order of a ruling upon its evidence is not valid as an interpretation of intellectual ibnā'; rather it is an example of it). He himself has acknowledged that 'tartīb al-ḥukm' is not the interpretation and definition of intellectual ibnā', but an example of it. The definition of intellectual ibnā' is something else: 'tartīb al-shay' 'alā shay' fī al-'aql' (the order of a thing upon a thing in the mind). And this definition applies perfectly to the order of thought upon known matters. Therefore, the author's definition is comprehensive and converse, and the objector's objection is frivolous.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of 'al-asl' (the origin) in Usul al-Fiqh, defending the author's definition against criticisms, especially from Imam al-Razi and later from Taftazani. The author, Sadr al-Shariah, defines al-asl as 'that upon which another thing is built' (ما يبتنى عليه غيره). This definition distinguishes al-asl from a mere necessary condition (muhtāj ilayh). The passage addresses four objections. First, that the definition also applies to the efficient cause (fā'il). The commentator answers that the author's definition intends material cause only, and the term 'asl' is not applied to the agent in Arabic usage; even if it were, other causes like formal and final are not covered, so al-Razi's definition (al-muhtāj ilayh) remains non-universal. Second, the definition's element 'ibnā' foundation is explained as foundational attribution, not causal efficacy, excluding the agent. Third, an apparent contradiction with the author's later statement in the chapter on metaphor is resolved: there 'muhtāj ilayh' is used only contextually to distinguish reality from metaphor, not as a universal definition. Fourth, Taftazani argues that the author's definition is not comprehensive because 'tartīb al-umūr al-ma'lūmah' (arrangement of known matters in thought) is an intellectual building that is neither sensory nor subsumed under 'tartīb al-ḥukm 'alā dalīlih'. The commentator rebuts that Taftazani himself admitted that 'tartīb al-ḥukm 'alā dalīlih' is merely an example, not the definition of intellectual building; the true definition is 'tartīb al-shay' 'alā shay' fī al-'aql', which applies to thought. Hence the author's definition is sound.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): That upon which another thing is built (ما يبتنى عليه غيره), not merely that which is needed.
محتاج الیہ (muhtāj ilayh): That which is needed, but not necessarily the foundational basis.
ابتناء (ibnā'): Construction or building of one thing upon another; either sensory (ḥissī) or intellectual ('aqlī).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author (Sadr al-Shariah), what is the correct definition of al-asl?
A) That which is needed (al-muhtāj ilayh)
B) That upon which another thing is built (ma yubtānā 'alayhi ghayruh)
C) The efficient cause (al-'illah al-fā'ilah)
D) The first principle of a science

Key Takeaway
Al-asl in Hanafi usul is the foundational basis upon which something is built, not a mere necessary condition — this precision is vital for correct analogical reasoning and textual interpretation.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
