اس اعتراض کے متعدد جوابات دیے گئے ہیں (۱) ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ اسماء منقولہ مشترک میں داخل نہیں بلکہ ہمارا دعوی ہے کہ یہ مشترک میں داخل ہیں لہذا تعریف ان پر صادق آنی چاہئے اور بعض حضرات کی تصریح ہمارے لیے حجت نہیں (۲) اگر اسماء منقولہ کومشترک میں داخل نہ کیا جائے تو پھر ہم جواب دیتے ہیں کہ مشترک کی تعریف ان پر صادق نہیں آتی کیونکہ مشترک کی تعریف میں ما وضع سے وضع لغوی مراد ہے اور اسماء منقولہ میں وضع لغوی متعدد نہیں ہوتی بلکہ ایک ہوتی ہے اور دوسری وضع یا شرعی ہوتی ہے عرفی وغیرہ لہذا اسماء منقولہ مشترک کی تعریف سے خارج ہو گئے (۳) یا یہ جواب دیا جا سکتا ہے کہ وضع کثیر سے مراد یہ ہے کہ من واضع واحد ہو یعنی تمام کا واضع ایک ہو یعنی واضع لغوی لہذا اسماء منقولہ خارج ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ ان میں واضع متعدد نہوتے ہیں یعنی ناقل شرعی یا عرفی یا نحوی و غیره (۴) یہ جواب بھی دیا جا سکتا ہے کہ مشترک کی تعریف میں وضع سے مراد وضع اولی اور ابتدائی ہے یعنی اس کی ابتدائی اور اولی وضع کثیر اور متعدد کیلئے ہوتی ہے بخلاف اسماء منقولہ کے کہ ان کی ابتدائی وضع کثیر کیلئے نہیں ہوتی بلکہ وضع ثانی ہوتی ہے لہذا یہ مشترک کی تعریف سے خارج ہو جائیں گے (۵) یہ جواب بھی دیا جا سکتا ہے کہ مشترک کی تعریف میں وضع شیر سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ وضع بلامحلل نقل ہو یعنی درمیان میں نقل کا واسطہ نہ ہو جبکہ اسماء منقولہ میں نقل کا واسطہ ہوتا ہے (۲) یہ جواب بھی دیا گیا ہے کہ اگر مشترک کی تعریف اسماء منقولہ پر صادق آ رہی ہے تو کوئی گناہ نہیں کیونکہ یہاں مشترک کو جمیع ماعداہ سے جدا کرنا مقصود نہیں ہے بلکہ تعریف سے مقصود باقی اقسام سے ممتاز کرنا ہے تو یہ تعریف ناقص ہے لہذا اس کا جامع مانع ہونا شرط نہیں ہے
Objection: The definition of mushtarak is not exclusive; it applies to transferred terms (asma' manqula) which were first placed for generic meanings and then transferred to technical meanings, by some suitability or without. For example, zakat lexically means absolute increase or purification, but the Law transferred it to another meaning: spending a portion of one's wealth in the path of Allah. Similarly, fi'l lexically means to do, but grammarians transferred it to a different meaning: a word that indicates a meaning in itself associated with one of the three times. The first meaning is called manqul 'anhu, the second manqul ilayhi. Likewise the word dawaran was placed for a generic meaning (i.e., turning) then transferred to another meaning (i.e., a ruling revolving with its 'illa). So in all these transferred terms, there are multiple wad's: first placed for one meaning, then placed for another meaning. Thus the definition of mushtarak applies to them, although they are not called mushtarak, as some scholars have explicitly stated that transferred terms are not included in mushtarak. Answers: Multiple answers have been given: (1) We do not accept that transferred terms are not included in mushtarak; rather they are included, so the definition should apply, and some scholars' specification is not proof for us. (2) If transferred terms are not included, then we answer that the definition of mushtarak does not apply because in its definition, 'wad'' refers to linguistic wad', and in transferred terms there is not multiple linguistic wad' but only one, and the second wad' is either shar'i or 'urfi etc., so they are excluded. (3) Or it can be answered that by 'multiple wad'' is meant that the wadi' (positor) is one, i.e., the linguistic positor; so transferred terms are excluded because they have multiple positors (the Lawgiver, custom, grammarian etc.). (4) Or that in the definition of mushtarak, 'wad'' refers to the first and original wad', i.e., its first/original wad' is for multiple meanings, unlike transferred terms whose first wad' is not for multiple, but the second wad' is, so they are excluded. (5) Or that by 'wad'' is meant wad' without an intervening transfer, i.e., no medium of naql; transferred terms have a medium of naql. (6) If the definition of mushtarak applies to transferred terms, there is no harm, because here the aim is not to separate mushtarak from everything else, but only to distinguish it from other categories; thus the definition is deficient, so it does not need to be jami' mani'.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a scholastic objection and response about the definition of mushtarak (homonym). The objection: the definition of mushtarak (a word placed for multiple meanings, each with its own wad') would incorrectly include transferred terms (manqulat) like zakat, fi'l, dawaran, because they too have multiple wad' (original and transferred). Yet scholars say they are not mushtarak. The author presents five or six answers from the Hanafi usul tradition. The first answer simply rejects the premise—some Hanafis do consider manqulat as mushtarak. The second distinguishes between linguistic wad' (which is singular for manqulat) and subsequent shar'i/'urfi wad', so the definition's 'wad'' refers only to linguistic wad'. The third emphasizes oneness of the wadi': mushtarak requires a single positor; manqulat involve multiple positors (the Lawgiver or custom). The fourth distinguishes first/original wad' versus second: mushtarak's first wad' is for multiple; manqulat's first wad' is for one, second for another. The fifth requires that wad' be without intervening transfer; manqulat have such an intervening transfer. The sixth concedes that the definition may be deficient in coverage, but since it is merely distinguishing from other types, it need not be strictly jami' mani'.

Key Terms
مشترک (mushtarak): لفظ وضع لمعان متعددة لكل واحد منها وضع على حدة
منقول (manqul): لفظ وضع أولا لمعنى ثم نقل إلى معنى آخر بمناسبة أو بدونها
وضع (wad'): تخصيص لفظ لمعنى

Checkpoint
According to the second answer in the passage, why are manqulat excluded from mushtarak?
A) Because manqulat have only one meaning
B) Because manqulat have multiple linguistic wad's
C) Because the definition of mushtarak refers only to linguistic wad', and manqulat have only one linguistic wad'
D) Because manqulat are not Arabic terms

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi exclusion of manqulat from mushtarak hinges on restricting wad' to linguistic wad' or requiring a single wadi' or absence of intervening transfer.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Definition of 'Amm: Conditions and Distinction from Mushtarak and Asma' 'Adad
Explaining the definition of 'amm and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'amm, identify its three conditions, and distinguish it from mushtarak and asma' 'adad by explaining the difference in wad'.

Core Idea
Amm has one wad' for a universal meaning covering all individuals; mushtarak has multiple wad's.

The classical Hanafi definition of 'amm ('general') is a precise legal tool: it is a word placed with a single wad' for many unlimited individuals, encompassing all that it applies to. This lesson unpacks each condition — wad'an wahidan, kathir ghayr mahsur, istighraq — and shows how they exclude mushtarak, indefinite nouns, and numerical nouns. Understanding this definition is foundational to applying Hanafi usul al-fiqh, where 'amm is treated as qat'i until specified.

Guided Path
1
Break down the definition's components
The definition has four parts: word, single wad', many unlimited, encompassing all. Identify each component and its role.
This is a standard Hanafi definition of 'amm found in works like Al-Tawdih.
2
Analyze the function of 'wad'an wahidan'
Determine whether this condition excludes mushtarak or is merely clarifying. The commentator notes a closer-to-truth view that it is for clarification, because mushtarak is already excluded by istighraq.
This reflects Hanafi precision in definitional conditions.
3
Understand 'istighraq' and its types
Istighraq can be comprehensive (shumul) as in collective nouns, or alternating (badal) as in conditionals. The passage addresses whether mushtarak has istighraq badali.
Hanafis require actual istighraq, not mere possibility.
4
Distinguish from mushtarak
Mushtarak has multiple wad's for different meanings; 'amm has one wad' for a universal meaning. The difference is in the nature of the wad'.
Example: 'ayn is mushtarak (eye, spring, etc.); 'rijal' is 'amm.
5
Distinguish from asma' 'adad
Numerical nouns (e.g., 'khamsah') are placed for a limited number, so they are excluded by 'ghayr mahsur' (unlimited).
The distinction lies in the limit of applicability.

یہ ہوتا ہے کہ مشترک عام اور اسماء عدد ہر ایک کی تعریف میں وضع للکثیر کا ذکر ہے مشترک میں بھی وضع لکثیر ہے عام کی تعریف میں بھی ما وضع وضعا واحد الکثیر ہے اسی طرح اسماء عدد کی وضع بھی کثیر محصور کیلئے ہے تو جب ان تمام تعریفات میں وضع لکثیر کا ذکر ہے تو ان تینوں میں فرق کیسے ہوگا۔ والمراد سے شارح اس کی تو جید و جواب پیش کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر چہ ان تمام میں وضع لکثیر کا ذکر ہے لیکن تینوں میں فرق ہے مشترک میں وضع لکثیر کا مطلب یہ ہوتا ہے کہ مشترک کے افراد میں ہے ہر ہر فرد کیلئے لفظ کی وضع ہوتی ہے لہذا اس میں مشترک کا ہر ہر فرد عین معنی موضوع نہ ہوگا جیسے لفظ میں اپنے معانی متعددہ و افراد متعددہ میں سے ہر ایک کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے لہذا عین کا ہر معنی لفظ عین کیلئے موضوع نہ ہوگا اور عام کی وضع لکثیر کا مطلب یہ ہوتا ہے کہ عام کی وضع ایک معنی کلی و مفہوم کلی کیلئے ہوتی ہے جس میں اس کے تمام افراد شریک ہوتے ہیں لہذا عام کا ہر ہر فرد عین موضوع لہ تو نہیں بنے گا البتہ موضوع لہ کے جزئیات میں سے ایک جزئی بنے گا جیسے رجل کی وضع مفہوم کلی ( حد صفر سے
His statement: 'Al-'amm is a word placed with a single wad' for many unlimited individuals, encompassing all that it applies to.' So his saying 'with a single wad'' (wad'an wahidan) — the commentator explains the benefits and conditions of the definition of 'amm: 'wad'an wahidan' is the first distinguishing condition (fasl) — by it mushtarak is excluded when its relation is to multiple meanings. If its relation is to individuals of a single meaning, then it remains included in the definition of 'amm, like the word 'man' for individuals of a genus. By 'wa qurba an yuqala' the commentator explains that the closer to the truth is that the condition of 'wad'an wahidan' is not for exclusion but only for clarification and explanation, because mushtarak is later excluded by the condition of 'istighraq' (summation), since mushtarak does not encompass all its meanings but only intends one meaning at a time. If it is said: the intended meaning of istighraq [is problematic] — an objection that mushtarak is not excluded by the condition of istighraq because istighraq has a division: istighraq 'ala sabil al-shumul (comprehensive) like in forms of jam' and ism jam' (e.g., al-rijal, al-qawm) or istighraq 'ala sabil al-badal (alternating) like 'whoever enters my house, for him such-and-such'. And mushtarak also has istighraq 'ala sabil al-badal, so it would not be excluded by istighraq. We (qulna) answer that istighraq with 'umum is not correct, otherwise the negative indefinite (nakira muthbata?) would also enter the definition of 'amm because it also encompasses every individual on an alternating basis. If it is said: it is not placed for many — an objection to the commentator's answer: although the positive indefinite encompasses on an alternating basis, it is not placed for many, so it would be excluded by the condition of 'kathir'. We answer: firstly we do not accept that the positive indefinite is not placed for many; even if we accept, your answer applies only to singular indefinite, not to plural indefinite (jam' nakira) because it is placed for many and encompasses all individuals on an alternating basis according to those who do not hold its generality. So the plural indefinite would enter the definition of 'amm, although according to those who deny generality, it is not 'amm. And the intended meaning by 'al-wad' li al-kathir' is the wad' for each individual of the many... Purpose: answer to an expected question. Question: In the definitions of mushtarak, 'amm, and nouns of number (asma' 'adad), each mentions wad' li al-kathir: mushtarak also has wad' li al-kathir, 'amm's definition also has 'wad'an wahidan li al-kathir', similarly nouns of number are placed for a limited number. So when all these definitions mention wad' li al-kathir, how is the distinction between them? By 'wa al-murad' the commentator gives explanation and answer: although all mention wad' li al-kathir, there is a difference among the three. In mushtarak, wad' li al-kathir means that for each individual of the kathir, there is a separate wad' for the word, so each individual of mushtarak is not exactly the object of wad' (al-wada' lii); rather it is for each meaning. For general ('amm), wad' li al-kathir means that the general's wad' is for a single universal meaning (ma'na kulli) in which all its individuals share, so each individual of the general is not itself the object of wad', but one particular of the object of wad'. For example, 'rajul' is placed for a universal meaning.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of 'amm (general) as given in the matn: 'A word placed with a single wad' for many unlimited individuals, encompassing all that it applies to.' The commentator explains each condition. 'Wad'an wahidan' (single wad') distinguishes 'amm from mushtarak when the mushtarak relates to multiple meanings; but if mushtarak relates to individuals of a single meaning (like man for individuals of a genus), it is not excluded by this condition. However, the commentator notes that the closer-to-truth view is that 'wad'an wahidan' is not for exclusion but for clarification, because mushtarak is already excluded later by the condition of istighraq (encompassing all that it applies to), since mushtarak does not encompass all its meanings simultaneously but only picks one. Then an objection arises: mushtarak does have istighraq on an alternating basis (badal), so it would not be excluded. The reply: if we accept that, then the indefinite (nakira) would also enter, but some argue that indefinite is not placed for 'many' (kathir), so it is excluded by that condition. The commentator discusses that plural indefinite (jam' nakira) is placed for many and thus might enter, but those who deny its generality would not consider it 'amm. Finally, the passage distinguishes the three terms: mushtarak (wad' for each individual separately), 'amm (wad' for a universal meaning covering all individuals), and asma' 'adad (wad' for a limited number). Thus the difference lies in how the 'kathir' is understood.

Key Terms
عام ('amm): لفظ وضع وضعا واحدا لكثير غير محصور مستغرق جميع ما يصلح له
وضعا واحدا (wad'an wahidan): وضع واحد للفظ لمعنى كلي يشمل جميع أفراده
استغراق (istighraq): شمول اللفظ لجميع ما يصلح له، إما على سبيل الشمول أو البدل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the closer-to-truth view about the function of 'wad'an wahidan' in the definition of 'amm?
A) It excludes mushtarak when the mushtarak relates to multiple meanings
B) It excludes mushtarak when the mushtarak relates to individuals of a single meaning
C) It is not for exclusion but for clarification and explanation only
D) It excludes the indefinite (nakira) from the definition

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'amm hinges on a single wad' for a universal meaning, distinguishing it from mushtarak and numerical nouns.

Including Nakira Manfiya in the Definition of 'Amm
Defending inclusion of nakira manfiya in definition of 'amm via wad' naw'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of wad' (shakhsi and naw'i), apply the concept of wad' naw'i to explain the generality of nakira manfiya, and evaluate objections against its inclusion in the definition of 'amm.

Core Idea
Nakira manfiya gains genuine generality through wad' naw'i, not mere rational inference or metaphor.

This passage defends the Hanafi definition of 'amm as 'a word posited for a multitude without limit' and argues that nakira manfiya belongs to this category. The commentator uses a question-and-answer format to address objections, distinguishing between personal and type-based linguistic positing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of 'amm
State the Hanafi definition: a word posited for a multitude (kathir) without limit (ghayr mahsur).
This definition emphasizes wad' (positing) as the basis for generality.
2
Understand the objections to including nakira manfiya
List the objections the passage addresses: (a) proper names like Zayd would also be included due to parts, (b) nakira manfiya is not posited for a multitude, (c) its generality is rational not wad'i, (d) it is metaphorical not literal.
These objections challenge the definition's scope and the nature of nakira manfiya's generality.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response using wad' types
The commentator introduces wad' shakhsi (personal positing) and wad' naw'i (type positing). Nakira manfiya's generality arises from wad' naw'i, a general rule derived from consistent usage.
Wad' naw'i explains how a class of words acquires a common meaning.
4
Distinguish between rational and wad'i generality
The responder argues that wad' naw'i itself is based on rational deduction from usage, so there is no conflict between the rational and wad'i aspects.
This reconciles the objection that the generality is merely rational.
5
Evaluate the final ruling on nakira manfiya
Conclude that nakira manfiya is included in 'amm because its generality is literal and rooted in wad' naw'i, not metaphorical or purely rational.
This upholds the Hanafi position that all forms of 'amm, including nakira manfiya, share the same definition.

The discussion concerns the definition of 'amm (general) and whether nakira manfiya (negated indefinite) is included. Objection: If 'amm is defined as 'posited for a multitude', then proper names like Zayd, Amr, and common nouns like man, horse would also be included because they have parts. Answer: The relevant multitude is of parts that share the same name, like units of a hundred; each is called 'one of the hundred', similar to individuals of a universal. Zayd and Amr lack such parts. Objection: Nakira manfiya is considered 'amm by usuliyun, but it is not posited for a multitude because it negates a specific individual. Answer: Wad' (positing) includes wad' shakhsi (personal) and wad' naw'i (type). Nakira manfiya has wad' naw'i derived from the general rule that every negated indefinite in the context of negation yields generality, as evidenced by the consistent usage of usuliyun. Thus, nakira manfiya's wad' naw'i is for a multitude without limit. Objection: Its generality is rational ('aqli), not wad'i. Answer: There is no conflict because wad' naw'i is based on rational deduction. Objection: Its generality is metaphorical (majaz). Answer: It is literal (haqiqah) because nakira manfiya has both wad' shakhsi for the specific individual and wad' naw'i for the negation of all individuals, as confirmed by commentators of Ibn al-Hajib's Mukhtasar. Finally, objection: 'Ghayr mahsur' (unlimited) might mean infinite, but this is false because creation is finite. The answer is that 'ghayr mahsur' here means indefinite in number, not infinite.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) defending the definition of 'amm (general) as 'a word posited for a multitude without limit' and arguing that nakira manfiya (negated indefinite, e.g., 'no man') falls under this definition. The author addresses three objections: (1) Proper names and common nouns seem to have parts but are excluded because the required multitude must share the same name uniformly (like units of a hundred). (2) Nakira manfiya is not posited for a multitude, but the author explains that wad' includes both wad' shakhsi (specific pairing, like 'Zayd' for a person) and wad' naw'i (a general rule, like 'every word on the pattern fa'il means the doer'). Nakira manfiya's generality arises from wad' naw'i: usuliyun consistently use it to negate all individuals, establishing a general rule. (3) Some argue its generality is rational, not posited; the author replies that wad' naw'i is itself derived from rational observation, so no conflict. (4) Some claim the generality is metaphorical; the author asserts it is literal because nakira manfiya has both a personal positing (for a specific individual) and a type positing (for negation of all). The passage follows a question-and-answer format, typical of this sharh. Key concepts: wad' shakhsi, wad' naw'i, and the distinction between 'amm haqiqi and 'amm hukmi.

Key Terms
العام (al-amm): A word posited for a multitude (kathir) without limit (ghayr mahsur).
النكرة المنفية (al-nakira al-manfiya): An indefinite noun in a negative context (e.g., لا رجل 'no man'). Its generality comes from wad' naw'i, not wad' shakhsi.
الوضع الشخصي (al-wad' al-shakhsi): Positing a specific word for a specific meaning, e.g., the word 'Zayd' for the person Zayd.
الوضع النوعي (al-wad' al-naw'i): Positing a general rule that applies to a class of words, e.g., every word on a certain pattern has a meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What two types of wad' (positing) does the author distinguish, and which one applies to nakira manfiya's generality?
A) Wad' shakhsi and wad' naw'i; nakira manfiya has wad' naw'i.
B) Wad' haqiqi and wad' majazi; nakira manfiya has wad' haqiqi.
C) Wad' 'amm and wad' khass; nakira manfiya has wad' 'amm.
D) Wad' lughawi and wad' shar'i; nakira manfiya has wad' shar'i.

Key Takeaway
Nakira manfiya is a genuine 'amm because its generality is rooted in a type of linguistic positing (wad' naw'i), not merely rational or metaphorical.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Generality of the Negative Indefinite: Wad'i Naw'i vs 'Aqli
Explaining the nature of generality in negative indefinite nouns and reconciling wad'i and 'aqli perspectives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the negative indefinite's generality is both a rational necessity and a type placement (wad'i naw'i), and resolve the apparent conflict between these two aspects.

Core Idea
The negative indefinite's generality is both rational necessity and type placement—no conflict.

In Hanafi usul, the rule that a negative indefinite (nakira manfiyya) conveys generality of negation is a foundational principle. But is this generality from the word's original placement (wad') or from rational necessity? This lesson unpacks the passage where the commentator reconciles both, showing that the wad'i naw'i is itself derived from a rational rule, so there is no contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about the negative indefinite
The passage states that usuli scholars use the negative indefinite wherever they want to negate a ruling from all individuals. The term 'wad'i naw'i' is applied to this usage, meaning that the word is considered placed for this purpose by a general rule.
2
Understand the rational objection
An objector argues that the indefinite (nakira) is originally placed for a specific unspecified individual (fard muhm). Therefore, its negation only directly negates that individual; the extension to all individuals is not from wad' but is a rational necessity (since negating an unspecified individual is impossible unless all are negated). Hence, the generality is 'aqli (rational), not wad'i.
3
Follow the commentator's response
The commentator replies that there is no opposition between wad'i naw'i and rational generality, because the general rule that proves the wad'i naw'i is itself derived from reason. Thus the wad'i naw'i is established on a rational basis, and both aspects coexist harmoniously.
4
Distinguish wad'i naw'i from wad'i shakhsi
Wad'i shakhsi is the initial placement of a word for a specific meaning. Wad'i naw'i, by contrast, is a secondary placement that emerges from a rational rule applied to the word in certain contexts (like negation). This distinction resolves the apparent conflict.
Hanafi usul often relies on such type placements for deriving general rules.
5
Apply the concept to fiqh examples
Whenever a mujtahid encounters a negative indefinite in a primary text (Quran or Hadith), he applies this rule to derive a general negation. For instance, the hadith 'لا صلاة لجار المسجد إلا في المسجد' (no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque) uses a negative indefinite (صلاة) and is interpreted as negating the validity of any prayer outside the mosque for such a person.

منفیہ میں وضع نوعی کو بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ علماء اصولین نکرہ منفیہ کو جہاں بھی استعمال کرتے ہیں وہاں حکم کی نفی ہوتی ہے کثیر غیر محصور افراد ہے اور نکرہ منفیہ والا لفظ نفی والے حکم میں ہر ہر فرد کو مستغرق ہوتا ہے یعنی اس میں عموم نفی ہوتا ہے ( یعنی نفی عام ہوتی ہے ) اگر نکرہ منفیہ مفرد ہو تو نفی تمام افراد سے ہوتی ہے اگر نکرہ منفیہ جمع ہو تو نفی مجموع سے ہوتی ہے لا یفی العموم یعنی نکرہ منفیہ عموم نفی کے لیے آتا ہے نفی عموم کے لیے نہیں آتا یعنی اس کا یہ مراد نہیں ہوتا کہ حکم تمام افراد کو شامل نہیں ہے بعض کو شامل ہے بعض کو نہیں جسے سلب شمول کہا جاتا ہے نکرہ منفیہ کا یہ مفہوم نہیں ہوتا تو حضرات اصولیین کی استعمال سے ایک قاعدہ کلیہ مستنبط ہوا کہ ہر نکرہ منفیہ عموم نفی کا فائدہ دیتا ہے تو گویا نکرہ منفیہ کو عموم نفی کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہے اس کو وضع نوعی کہا جاتا ہے تو نکرہ منفیہ کی وضع نوعی لکثیر غیر محصور پائی گئی ہے لہذا عام کی تعریف اس پر صادق آ رہی ہے۔ وکون عمومها عقليا ضروريا الخ غرض جواب سوال مقدر سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ آپ نے نکرہ منفیہ کے اندر عموم وضعی نوعی ثابت کیا ہے حالانکہ اس میں عموم وضعی نہیں ہے بلکہ عقلی ضروری ( بدیہی ہے کیونکہ نکرہ کی وضع فرد مہم کے لیے ہوتی ہے اور نکرہ منفیہ میں نفی فرد مہم کی ہوتی ہے اور فرد مہم کی نفی اس وقت تک عقلا محال ہے جب تک ہر ہر فرد کی نفی نہ ہو تو ثابت ہوا کہ نکرہ منفیہ میں جو عموم نفی ہوتا ہے وہ عقل ہے بداہتہ ثابت ہوتا ہے وضع سے ثابت نہیں ہے لہذا یہ عموم وضعی نوعی نہیں ہے بلکہ عقلی ہے شارح جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ وضع نوعی اور عقلی میں کوئی منافات نہیں ہے کیونکہ وضع نوعی جس قاعدہ کلیہ کے تحت ثابت ہو رہی ہے وہ قاعدہ عقل سے ہی مستنبط ہو تا ہے لہذا فلا منافاة ولا تعارض بینھما
In the negative [indefinite], they are explaining the wad'i naw'i: that the usuli scholars wherever they use the negative indefinite, there is a negation of the ruling, many non-limited individuals, and the word of the negative indefinite in the negative ruling encompasses every individual, meaning it has generality of negation (i.e., general negation). If the negative indefinite is singular, then negation is from all individuals; if the negative indefinite is plural, then negation is from the totality. It does not indicate generality, meaning the negative indefinite comes for the generality of negation, not for the negation of generality. That is, it is not meant that the ruling does not include all individuals but includes some and not others, which is called negation of inclusion; the negative indefinite does not have this meaning. So from the usage of the usuli scholars, a general rule was derived that every negative indefinite gives the benefit of generality of negation. So it is as if the negative indefinite was placed for the generality of negation; this is called wad'i naw'i. Thus the wad'i naw'i of the negative indefinite is found for many non-limited individuals, so the definition of 'amm applies to it. 'And that its generality is rational necessary, etc.' The purpose is the answer to an implied question: The question is that you have proven a wad'i naw'i generality in the negative indefinite, whereas it does not have wad'i generality but rather rational necessary (intuitive) because the wad' of the indefinite is for a specific individual, and in the negative indefinite the negation is of a specific individual, and the negation of a specific individual is rationally impossible unless the negation of every individual occurs. So it is proven that the generality of negation in the negative indefinite is [by] reason, proven intuitively, not proven by wad'. Therefore this is not wad'i naw'i generality but rational. The commentator replies that there is no opposition between wad'i naw'i and rational, because the general rule under which the wad'i naw'i is proven is itself derived from reason. So there is no opposition or contradiction between them.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of 'amm (general), focusing on the case of the negative indefinite (al-nakira al-manfiyya). The commentator begins by explaining the position that the negative indefinite conveys generality of negation, meaning that it negates the ruling from every individual (in the singular) or from the totality (in the plural). This is a general rule derived from the usage of the usuli scholars. The term 'wad'i naw'i' (general designation by type) is applied because the word is said to be placed for this purpose. However, an objection is raised: the indefinite (nakira) is originally placed for a specific individual (fard muhm), so its negation is only of a specific individual; the generality to all individuals is not from the wad' but is a rational necessity (since negating a specific unspecified individual is impossible unless all individuals are negated). The commentator responds that there is no conflict: the wad'i naw'i is proven by a general rule that itself is derived from reason. Thus both aspects are valid and consistent.

Key Terms
وضع نوعی (wad'i naw'i): A designation that makes a word convey a general meaning by virtue of a rule derived from reason, not from the initial individual placement.
عموم عقلی (umum 'aqli): Generality that is rationally necessary, not linguistically placed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the relationship between the wad'i naw'i and rational ('aqli) generality in the negative indefinite?
A) They are contradictory; one negates the other.
B) They are compatible; the wad'i naw'i is based on a rule derived from reason.
C) The wad'i naw'i is not applicable to the negative indefinite.
D) Rational generality is a subcategory of wad'i naw'i.

Key Takeaway
The negative indefinite's generality of negation is both a rational necessity and a type placement (wad'i naw'i) in Hanafi usul, with no conflict between the two.

Generality of the Negative Indefinite: Haqiqi Not Majaz
Refuting the claim that negative indefinite generality is metaphorical

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers the generality of the negative indefinite as real (haqiqi) and distinguish between wad' shakhsi and wad' naw'i in this context.

Core Idea
The negative indefinite's generality is real because of wad' naw'i, not a metaphorical extension.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a potential objection: if the negative indefinite's literal meaning is only negation of a specific individual, its generality would be metaphorical, and thus it would not be a true 'amm. The Hanafi response clarifies that there is a real type-based placement (wad' naw'i) that arises from the context of negation, making the generality real. This distinction is crucial for defining 'amm in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
What is the claim that the generality in the negative indefinite is metaphorical? Understand the opponent's reasoning: the literal meaning is only negation of a specific individual, so generality is secondary and metaphorical.
The opponent argues that the definition of 'amm is for real general terms, so this would exclude the negative indefinite.
2
State the Hanafi refutation
The commentator says "لا نسلم" (we do not accept). This is the classical term for rejecting a premise in a debate. The Hanafi position is that the generality is not metaphorical but real.
3
Differentiate wad' shakhsi and wad' naw'i
wad' shakhsi is the original placement for a specific individual. wad' naw'i is a secondary but real placement arising from the context of negation: the wadi' intended that every indefinite under negation becomes general.
The wad' naw'i is a real designation, not a metaphorical extension.
4
Understand how wad' naw'i makes generality real
Because the indefinite is under negation, the negation applies to every individual of that kind. This is a real linguistic function, not a figurative one.
5
Note supporting evidence
The commentator cites commentators of Ibn al-Hajib's Mukhtasar, who explicitly state that the generality in the negative indefinite is real (haqiqah), not metaphorical.
This strengthens the Hanafi argument by relying on established usul texts.

لا يقال النكرة المنفية مجاز والتعريف للعام الحقيقي غرض جواب سوال ۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ نکرہ منفیہ میں جو عموم آتا ہے وہ مجازی ہے کیونکہ حقیقت میں نکرہ منفیہ موضوع ہے فرد مہم کی نفی کے لیے عموم تو بعد میں مجاز آتا ہے اور یہاں تعریف عام حقیقی کی کی جارہی ہے لہذا یہ عام کی تعریف میں داخل نہ ہو گا ؟ لا نسلم سے جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ نکرہ منفیہ میں عموم مجازی ہے بلکہ عموم وضعی حقیقی ہے بلکہ نکرہ منفیہ میں تو وضع شخصی بھی ہے وضع نوعی بھی کیونکہ واضع نے اس کو وضع کیا ہے فرد مہم کے لیے تو فرد مہم اس کا معنی موضوع لہ بالوضع الشخصی ہوگا در حقیقت نکرہ منفیہ اپنے اس معنی موضوع لہ فرد مہم میں استعمال ہوتا ہے البتہ نکرہ تحت النفی ہونے کی وجہ سے پھر اس میں عموم نفی پیدا ہو جاتا ہے کہ ہر ہر فرد سے نفی ہو جاتی ہے تو یہ وضع نوعی ہوگئی گویا واضع نے یوں قصد کیا کہ ہر نکرہ جو تحت النفی واقع ہو تو نفی میں عام ہو گا اس کی تائید کے لیے فرمایا کہ اصول ابن الحاجب کے شارحین نے بھی تصریح کی ہے کہ نکرہ منفیہ میں عموم حقیقت ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مجاز و معنى كون الكثير غير محصورا الخ
It cannot be said that the negative indefinite is metaphorical and the definition is for the real general. Purpose: answer to an implied question. The question is: The generality that occurs in the negative indefinite is metaphorical, because in reality the negative indefinite is placed for negation of a specific individual; generality then comes metaphorically. And here the definition of the real general is being given, so it will not be included in the definition of 'amm. [The commentator] answers with 'we do not accept' that we do not accept that the generality in the negative indefinite is metaphorical; rather it is real wad'i generality. In fact, the negative indefinite has both wad' shakhsi and wad' naw'i. Because the wadi' placed it for a specific individual, so the specific individual is its meaning placed for by wad' shakhsi. In reality, the negative indefinite is used in its meaning placed for, the specific individual. However, due to being indefinite under negation, then the generality of negation is generated in it, so that negation occurs from every individual. This becomes wad' naw'i, as if the wadi' intended that every indefinite that occurs under negation becomes general in negation. In support of this, he said that the commentators of usul of Ibn al-Hajib also explicitly stated that generality in the negative indefinite is real, not metaphorical. 'And the meaning of it being many non-limited, etc.'
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the negative indefinite. The commentator addresses a potential objection: the generality in the negative indefinite might be considered metaphorical (majaz), because the literal meaning is only negation of a specific individual. If so, it would not be included in the definition of 'amm, which is defined for real (haqiqi) general terms. The commentator refutes this by asserting that the generality is not metaphorical but real. He distinguishes between two types of wad': wad' shakhsi (individual placement) for the specific individual, and wad' naw'i (type placement) that arises from the context of negation. The wad' naw'i is a secondary but real designation. He supports this by citing the commentators of Ibn al-Hajib, who confirm that generality in negative indefinite is real (haqiqah), not metaphorical.

Key Terms
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage; where the word is used in a meaning other than its original wad' without being the intended meaning.
وضع شخصی (wad' shakhsi): Individual placement; the original designation of the word for a specific individual.
وضع نوعی (wad' naw'i): Type placement; a secondary but real designation that arises from a specific context (e.g., negation) and gives generality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is the generality in the negative indefinite considered real (haqiqi) rather than metaphorical (majazi)?
A) Because the literal meaning is negation of every individual.
B) Because it has a wad' naw'i that arises from the context of negation.
C) Because scholars have declared it metaphorical and then reinterpreted it.
D) Because it is used in poetry and figurative speech.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms that the generality of the negative indefinite is real (haqiqi), not metaphorical, due to the existence of wad' naw'i arising from the context of negation.

Meaning of 'Ghayr Mahsur' in the Definition of 'Amm
Clarifying the condition 'ghayr mahsur' in the definition of 'amm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct meaning of 'ghayr mahsur' and apply it to distinguish 'amm from other expressions.

Core Idea
Ghayr mahsur in 'amm means no qarina to a specific number, not infinite individuals.

The condition 'ghayr mahsur' (non-limited) in the definition of 'amm often causes confusion. Some assume it implies that the individuals covered are infinite, while others think it means they are uncountable. In this passage, the commentator clarifies that the correct meaning is the absence of a contextual indicator (qarina) specifying a particular number. This nuance is essential for correctly identifying 'amm and excluding terms like numbers (asma' 'adad) from the definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the implied question
The passage begins with an implied question: If many individuals are non-limited, does that mean the word is placed for infinite individuals? Recognize why this question arises from a literal reading of 'ghayr mahsur'.
2
Understand the correct meaning of 'ghayr mahsur'
The commentator clarifies that 'non-limited' does not mean infinite. Instead, it means the word itself lacks a qarina indicating a specific number. Many existing individuals are finite, but the word's generality remains.
3
Analyze Taftazani's refutation of an alternative interpretation
Some scholars interpreted 'ghayr mahsur' as 'not subject to counting'. Taftazani refutes this using two counterexamples: 'al-samawat' (heavens, countable yet 'amm) and 'alf alf' (a thousand thousand, uncountable yet not 'amm).
The first counterexample is supported by consensus (ijma).
4
Extract the core principle
From Taftazani's refutation, derive that the only valid meaning of 'ghayr mahsur' is the absence of a qarina indicating a specific number. This principle governs the application of 'amm.

و معنى كون الكثير غير محصورا الخ غرض شارح جواب سوال مقدر۔ سوال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ عام میں کہا گیا ہے وہ کثیر افراد کے لیے وضع کی گئی ہے اور کثیر افراد غیر محصور ہوتے ہیں اور غیر محصور بمعنی غیر متناہی ہے تو مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ عام اتنے کثیر افراد کے لیے وضع کی گئی ہے جن کی کوئی حد اور انتہاء ہی نہیں حالانکہ یہ تو باطل ہے کیونکہ کائنات میں جتنے بھی اشیاء کثیرہ موجود ہیں سب محصور و متناہی ہیں تو معنی کون الكثير غير محصورا سے شارح اس سوال کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ کثیر افراد کے غیر محصور ہونے کا یہ مطلب نہیں ہے کہ وہ کثیر افراد غیر متناہی ہوں بلکہ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس لفظ میں کوئی ایسا قرینہ نہ ہو جو عدد معین پر دلالت کر رہا ہو تو اس کو غیر محصور کہیں گے ورنہ تو کثیر موجود و متحقق افراد یقینا محصور ومتناہی ہوتے ہیں ۔لا يقال المراد بغير المحصور بعض حضرات نے غیر محصور کا ایک اور معنی کیا تھا تفتازانی ان کی رد کر رہے ہیں وہ یہ ہے کہ غیر محصور وہ اشیاء ہیں جو کسی ضبط اور شمار کے تحت داخل نہ ہوں تو تفتازانی کہتے ہیں یہ معنی غلط ہے ورنہ تو السموات جمع معرف باللام حصور ہو جائے گی کیونکہ یہ تحت الضبط والعد داخل ہے سموات سات ہیں لہذا یہ عام سے خارج ہو جائے گی حالانکہ السموات بالاتفاق عام ہے دوسری خرابی یہ لازم آئے گی کہ لفظ الف الف کثیر غیر محصور کے لیے ہے کیونکہ اس کا معنی ہے کئی ہزار تو یہ عدد تحت الضبط والعد نہیں آسکتا تو یہ غیر محصور ہو کر عام میں داخل ہو جائے گا حالانکہ بالاتفاق یہ عام نہیں ہے لہذا غیر محصور کا یہ معنی کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ لا یقال هذا القيد مستدرک غرض جواب سوال ۔ سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ عام کی تعریف میں غیر محصور کی قید لگانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس سے اسماء عدد خارج کرنا مقصود ہے اور اسماء عدد تو مستغرق للجميع ما يصلح له سے خارج ہو جاتے ہیں کیونکہ لفظ مائة وغیرہ من اسماء العدد یہ مائة کی جزئیات پر یعنی سینکڑے سینکڑے پر تو صادق آنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے لیکن مائة کے اجزاء و آحاد یعنی اکائیوں پر صادق آنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا جو مائة کے ضمن میں پائی جاتی ہیں کیونکہ ہر ایکائی کو مائة نہیں کہا جاتا جبکہ عام تو اپنے جزئیات و آحاد میں سے ہر ہر جزئی پر صادق آنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے جیسے رجال رجل کے ہر فرد پر صادق آنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے لہذا اسماء عدد مستغرق کی قید سے خارج ہو جاتے ہیں تو غیر محصور کی قید مستدرک ہے۔ لا نسلم سے جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ اسماء عدد مستغرق لجميع ما يصلح له سے خارج نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ جمیع ما يصلح له میں جس صلاحیت کا ذکر ہے اس میں تعمیم ہے خواہ کلی کی صلاحیت ہو اپنے جزئیات پر صادق آنے کی یا کل کی صلاحیت ہو اپنے اجزاء پر صادق آنے کی کلی اپنے جزئیات میں سے ہر جزئی پر صادق آتی ہے دلالت مطابقی کے ساتھ اور کل اپنے اجزاء میں سے ہر ہر جزء پر صادق آنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے دلالت تضمنی کے ساتھ لہذا دونوں میں جميع ما يصلح له پر صادق آنے کی صلاحیت موجود ہے خواہ دلالت مطابقی کے ساتھ ہو خواہ دلالت تضمنی کے ساتھ لہذا اسماء عدد مستغرق لجميع ما يصلح له سے خارج نہیں ہوں گے اور جمع اسم جمع رجال مسلمون رحط قوم سب عام میں داخل ہو جائیں گے اس لیے غیر محصور کی قید لگانے کی ضرورت تھی تا کہ اس سے اسماء عدد خارج ہو جائیں ۔ وقوله مستغرق مرفوع غرض مستغرق کا اعراب ضبط کر رہے ہیں کہ یہ مرفوع ہے اور لفظ کی صفت ہے اور استغراق لما یصلح لہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ لفظ ان تمام افراد پر دلالت کرے جن کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے خواہ
And the meaning of 'it being many non-limited, etc.' Purpose: the commentator's answer to an implied question. The question is: In 'amm it is said that it is placed for many individuals, and many individuals are non-limited, and non-limited means infinite, so the meaning would be that 'amm is placed for so many individuals that have no limit or end, but this is false because all the many things in the universe are limited and finite. So from 'the meaning of it being many non-limited', the commentator answers: The many individuals being non-limited does not mean that those many individuals are infinite; rather, it means that in this word there is no context (qarina) indicating a specific number, so it is called non-limited. Otherwise, the many existing and realized individuals are certainly limited and finite. It cannot be said: Some people have made another meaning of 'ghayr mahsur'. Taftazani refutes them: they said that 'ghayr mahsur' are things that are not subject to restriction and counting. Taftazani says this meaning is incorrect; otherwise 'al-samawat' (the heavens), which is a definite plural, would be limited because it is under restriction and count; the heavens are seven, so it would be excluded from 'amm, whereas 'al-samawat' is unanimously considered 'amm. Another defect is that the word 'alf alf' (a thousand thousand) would be for many non-limited because its meaning is several thousand; this number cannot come under restriction and counting, so it would become non-limited and included in 'amm, whereas it is unanimously not 'amm. Therefore this meaning of 'ghayr mahsur' is not correct. It cannot be said: This condition is redundant (mustadrak). Purpose: answer to a question. The question is: In the definition of 'amm, it is not necessary to add the condition 'ghayr mahsur' because the purpose is to exclude numbers (asma' 'adad), and numbers are already excluded by 'mustaghriq li-jami' ma yasluh lahu' because the word 'mi'a' etc. from numbers has the capability to apply to its parts, i.e., hundreds, but not to its parts and units, i.e., the ones that are found within a hundred, because each unit is not called a hundred. While 'amm has the capability to apply to every one of its particulars and units, like 'rijal' has the capability to apply to every individual man. Therefore numbers are excluded by the condition of 'istighraq', and the condition 'ghayr mahsur' is redundant. [The commentator] answers with 'we do not accept': numbers are not excluded by 'mustaghriq li-jami' ma yasluh lahu' because in 'jami' ma yasluh lahu' the capability mentioned is general: whether it is the capability of the universal (kulli) to apply to its particulars, or the capability of the whole (kull) to apply to its parts. The universal applies to every particular by dalalat mutabaqa, and the whole has the capability to apply to every part by dalalat tadammun. Therefore both have the capability to apply to 'jami' ma yasluh lahu', whether by dalalat mutabaqa or by dalalat tadammun. So numbers are not excluded by 'mustaghriq li-jami' ma yasluh lahu', and plural forms like 'rijal', 'muslimun', 'rahf', 'qaum' would all be included in 'amm. Thus it was necessary to add the condition 'ghayr mahsur' to exclude numbers. And his saying 'mustaghriq' is marfu' (nominative); he is indicating the vowel ending of 'mustaghriq': it is marfu', and it is an adjective of the word, and 'istighraq lima yasluh lahu' means that the word indicates all the individuals for which it has the potential, whether...
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage addresses three sub-discussions about the condition 'ghayr mahsur' (non-limited) in the definition of 'amm. First, it clarifies that 'ghayr mahsur' does not mean infinite, but rather that the word itself does not have a context (qarina) specifying a particular number. Second, Taftazani refutes an alternative interpretation that 'ghayr mahsur' means not subject to counting, providing counterexamples: 'al-samawat' (the heavens) is a definite plural which is counted (seven) yet is 'amm; and 'alf alf' (thousands) is not counted yet is not 'amm. Thus the correct meaning is the absence of a contextual indicator of a specific number. Third, an objection is raised that the condition is redundant because numbers (asma' 'adad) are already excluded by the condition 'mustaghriq li-jami' ma yasluh lahu' (encompassing all that it is suitable for). The commentator argues that numbers are not excluded because they have suitability for their parts (by implication) just as universal terms have suitability for their particulars (by correlation). Since numbers could be considered 'mustaghriq' by implication, the additional condition 'ghayr mahsur' is needed to exclude them. The passage ends with a grammatical note that 'mustaghriq' is marfu' (nominative) and describes the word.

Key Terms
غير محصور (ghayr mahsur): Not limited by a specific number; having no qarina indicating a particular number.
قرينة (qarina): A contextual indicator that specifies or restricts meaning.
السموات (al-samawat): The heavens; a definite plural used as a key counterexample.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct meaning of 'ghayr mahsur' in the Hanafi definition of 'amm?
A) The word refers to an infinite number of individuals.
B) The word refers to individuals that are not subject to counting.
C) The word does not have a contextual indicator specifying a particular number.
D) The word refers only to collective nouns.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'ghayr mahsur' means the absence of a qarina specifying a number, not infinite or uncountable individuals.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
10 min
Why the Condition 'Ghayr Mahsur' is Not Redundant
Defending the necessity of the condition 'ghayr mahsur' in the definition of 'amm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the condition 'ghayr mahsur' is necessary to exclude numbers (asma' 'adad) from the definition of 'amm.

Core Idea
Numbers are not excluded by 'mustaghriq' alone because they indicate their parts by implication, so 'ghayr mahsur' is needed.

An objection is raised that the condition 'ghayr mahsur' is redundant because numbers are already excluded by the condition 'mustaghriq li-jami' ma yasluh lahu' (encompassing all it is suitable for). The commentator rejects this by showing that numbers do have suitability for their parts by implicative indication (dalalat tadammun). Without 'ghayr mahsur', numbers would incorrectly be considered 'amm. This lesson explores the subtle interplay between the two conditions and why both are required.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector claims that 'ghayr mahsur' is unnecessary because numbers like 'mi'a' (hundred) are already excluded by the requirement that the word must apply to all its individuals (mustaghriq). The objector argues that 'mi'a' does not apply to each of its units (ones), so it fails the 'mustaghriq' condition.
2
Analyze the commentator's response
The commentator says 'we do not accept' (la nusallim). He argues that 'mustaghriq' includes both correlation (mutabaqa) and implication (tadammun). A number like 'mi'a' applies to its parts (the units) by implicative indication, because 'hundred' implies its units. Therefore, numbers do satisfy 'mustaghriq' and would be included in 'amm without 'ghayr mahsur'.
This shows that numbers can be considered 'encompassing' via tadammun.
3
See the consequence without 'ghayr mahsur'
If only 'mustaghriq' were present, then plural forms like 'rijal', 'muslimun', 'rahf', 'qaum' would be 'amm, but numbers would also be 'amm. This is unacceptable because numbers are not 'amm by consensus.
4
Conclude the necessity of the condition
Therefore, the condition 'ghayr mahsur' is essential to exclude numbers specifically, as they lack the 'non-limited' quality (they have an implicit numerical qarina).

Source Text

Commentary
This passage addresses three sub-discussions about the condition 'ghayr mahsur' (non-limited) in the definition of 'amm. First, it clarifies that 'ghayr mahsur' does not mean infinite, but rather that the word itself does not have a context (qarina) specifying a particular number. Second, Taftazani refutes an alternative interpretation that 'ghayr mahsur' means not subject to counting, providing counterexamples: 'al-samawat' (the heavens) is a definite plural which is counted (seven) yet is 'amm; and 'alf alf' (thousands) is not counted yet is not 'amm. Thus the correct meaning is the absence of a contextual indicator of a specific number. Third, an objection is raised that the condition is redundant because numbers (asma' 'adad) are already excluded by the condition 'mustaghriq li-jami' ma yasluh lahu' (encompassing all that it is suitable for). The commentator argues that numbers are not excluded because they have suitability for their parts (by implication) just as universal terms have suitability for their particulars (by correlation). Since numbers could be considered 'mustaghriq' by implication, the additional condition 'ghayr mahsur' is needed to exclude them. The passage ends with a grammatical note that 'mustaghriq' is marfu' (nominative) and describes the word.

Key Terms
مستغرق لما يصلح له (mustaghriq lima yasluh lahu): The word encompasses all that it is suitable for, whether by mutabaqa or tadammun.
دلالة تضمن (dalalat tadammun): Implicative indication; a word indicating its part by implication.
دلالة مطابقة (dalalat mutabaqa): Correlative indication; a word indicating its entire meaning directly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the condition 'ghayr mahsur' necessary in the definition of 'amm according to the commentator?
A) To exclude words like 'al-samawat' which are countable.
B) To exclude numbers like 'mi'a' and 'alf' which could otherwise be considered 'amm.
C) To ensure that the word is used in its metaphorical sense.
D) To include the negative indefinite in the definition.

Key Takeaway
The condition 'ghayr mahsur' is not redundant: it is essential to exclude numbers from being classified as 'amm.

Definition of 'Amm and the Condition of Ghayr Mahsur
Explains the definition of 'amm with the condition of being unlimited and defends its necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'amm, explain the condition of ghayr mahsur, and evaluate the objection that it is redundant.

Core Idea
The Hanafi 'amm requires both comprehensive indication and the absence of numerical limitation—both conditions are necessary.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih delves into the precise definition of 'amm in Hanafi usul. It clarifies what 'unlimited' really means, refutes a mistaken alternative, and defends the necessity of the condition to exclude numerical nouns. We will dissect the definition and the rational arguments surrounding it.

Guided Path
1
Identify key terms in the definition
Locate 'amm, istighraq, and ghayr mahsur in the source text. Understand their role in the definition.
2
Clarify the meaning of ghayr mahsur
The text explains that ghayr mahsur does not mean infinite; rather, it means the word has no contextual indicator (qarina) specifying a number.
3
Analyze the refutation of an alternative interpretation
Some defined ghayr mahsur as 'not subject to count/control.' The text refutes this using counterexamples: al-samawat is countable yet 'amm, and 'alf alf' is uncountable but not 'amm.
4
Understand the redundancy objection
An opponent argues that the condition ghayr mahsur is unnecessary because numerical nouns are already excluded by istighraq.
5
Follow the Hanafi response
The response shows that numerical nouns like 'mi'a' do have istighraq by implication (dalalat al-tadamun) over their parts, so they would not be excluded without the extra condition.
6
Note the grammatical adjustment
The word 'mustaghriq' in the definition is an adjective, marfu', modifying the term being defined.

اشیاء کثیرہ موجود ہیں سب محصور و متناہی ہیں تو معنی کون الکثیر محصورا سے شارح اس سوال کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ کثیر افراد کے غیر محصور ہونے کا یہ مطلب نہیں ہے کہ وہ کثیر افراد غیر متناہی ہوں بلکہ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس لفظ میں کوئی ایسا قرینہ نہ ہو جو عدد معین پر دلالت کر رہا ہو تو اس کو غیر محصور کہیں گے وگرنہ تو کثیر موجود و متحقق افراد یقینا محصور و متناہی ہوتے ہیں۔ لا یقال: المراد بغیر المحصور بعض حضرات نے غیر محصور کا ایک اور معنی کیا تھا تفتازانی ان کی رد کر رہے ہیں وہ یہ ہے کہ غیر محصور وہ اشیاء ہیں جو کسی ضبط اور شمار کے تحت داخل نہ ہوں تو تفتازانی کہتے ہیں یہ معنی غلط ہے ورنہ تو السموات جمع معرف باللام محصور ہو جائے گی کیونکہ یہ تحت الضبط والعد داخل ہے سموات سات ہیں لہذا یہ عام سے خارج ہو جائے گی حالانکہ السموات بالاتفاق عام ہے دوسری خرابی یہ لازم آئے گی کہ لفظ الف الف کثیر غیر محصور کے لیے ہے کیونکہ اس کا معنی ہے کئی ہزار تو یہ عدد تحت الضبط والعد [؟] (الشماء؟) نہیں آسکتا تو یہ غیر محصور ہو کر عام میں داخل ہو جائے گا حالانکہ بالاتفاق یہ عام نہیں ہے لہذا غیر محصور کا یہ معنی کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ لا یقال: هذا القید مستدرک غرض جواب سوال۔ سوال! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ عام کی تعریف میں غیر محصور کی قید لگانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس سے اسماء عدد خارج کرنا مقصود ہے اور اسماء عدد تو مستغرق لجمیع ما یصلح له سے خارج ہو جاتے ہیں کیونکہ لفظ مائۃ وغیرہ من اسماء العدد یہ مائۃ کی جزئیات پر یعنی سینکڑے سینکڑے پر تو صادق آنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے لیکن مائۃ کے اجزاء و آحاد یعنی اکائیوں پر صادق آنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا جو مائۃ کے ضمن میں پائی جاتی ہیں کیونکہ ہر ایک کو مائۃ نہیں کہا جاتا جبکہ عام تو اپنے جزئیات و آحاد میں سے ہر ہر جزئی پر صادق آنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے جیسے رجال رجل کے ہر فرد پر صادق آنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے لہذا اسماء عدد مستغرق کی قید سے خارج ہو جاتے ہیں تو غیر محصور کی قید مستدرک ہے۔ لانا نقول سے جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ اسماء عدد مستغرق لجمیع ما یصلح له سے خارج نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ جمیع ما یصلح له میں جس صلاحیت کا ذکر ہے اس میں تعمیم ہے خواہ کلی کی صلاحیت ہو اپنے جزئیات پر صادق آنے کی یا کل کی صلاحیت ہو اپنے اجزاء پر صادق آنے کی کلی اپنے جزئیات میں سے ہر جزئی پر صادق آتی ہے دلالت مطابقی کے ساتھ اور کل اپنے اجزاء میں سے ہر ہر جزء پر صادق آنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے دلالت تضمنی کے ساتھ لہذا دونوں میں جمیع ما یصلح له پر صادق آنے کی صلاحیت موجود ہے خواہ دلالت مطابقی کے ساتھ ہو خواہ دلالت تضمنی کے ساتھ لہذا اسماء عدد مستغرق لجمیع ما یصلح له سے خارج نہیں ہوں گے اور جمع اسم جمع رجال مسلمون رھط قوم سب عام میں داخل ہو جائیں گے اس لیے غیر محصور کی قید لگانے کی ضرورت تھی تا کہ اس سے اسماء عدد خارج ہو جائیں۔ وقوله مستغرق مرفوع غرض مستغرق کا اعراب ضبط کر رہے ہیں کہ یہ مرفوع ہے اور لفظ کی صفت ہے اور استغراق لما یصلح له کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ لفظ ان تمام افراد پر دلالت کرے جن کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے خواہ دلالت مطابقی ہو خواہ دلالت تضمنی
Many things exist, all are limited and finite. So the meaning of 'being many and limited' is that the commentator is answering this question: the fact that many individuals are not limited does not mean that those many individuals are infinite. Rather, its meaning is that there is no contextual indicator in that word indicating a specific number, so it is called 'unlimited'. Otherwise, many existing and realized individuals are certainly limited and finite. 'La yuqalu: al-murad bi-ghayr al-mahsur' Some people gave another meaning for 'non-limited'. Taftazani is refuting them. It is that 'non-limited' are things that do not fall under any control and count. Taftazani says this meaning is wrong; otherwise, 'al-samawat' (the heavens) with the definite article 'al-' would be limited because it falls under control and count: the heavens are seven. So it would be excluded from 'amm, although 'al-samawat' is by consensus 'amm. Another corruption would arise: the word 'alf alf' (a thousand thousand) is for a large number that is not limited? because its meaning is 'several thousand'. This number cannot fall under control and count [؟], so it would become non-limited and enter into 'amm, but by consensus it is not 'amm. Therefore, this meaning of 'non-limited' is not correct. 'La yuqalu: hadha al-qayd mustadrak' This is a question: The condition of putting 'non-limited' in the definition of 'amm is not necessary, because by it the intention is to exclude numerical nouns, and numerical nouns are already excluded from 'mustaghriq li-jami'i ma yasluhu lahu' because the word 'mi'a' etc. from numerical nouns applies to the particulars of a hundred, i.e., hundreds, but it does not have the capacity to apply to the parts and units of a hundred, i.e., ones, which are included within a hundred, because each one is not called a hundred. While 'amm has the capacity to apply to every single one of its particulars and units, such as 'rijal' has the capacity to apply to every individual man. Therefore, numerical nouns are excluded by the condition of 'istighraq', so the condition of 'non-limited' is superfluous. 'Lana naqulu' we respond: Numerical nouns are not excluded from 'mustaghriq li-jami'i ma yasluhu lahu' because in 'jami'i ma yasluhu lahu' the capacity mentioned includes generality, whether it is the capacity of the universal (kulli) to apply to its particulars, or the capacity of the whole (kull) to apply to its parts. The universal applies to every one of its particulars by the 'dalalat al-mutabaqah', and the whole has the capacity to apply to every part of its parts by the 'dalalat al-tadamun'. Thus, both have the capacity to apply to 'jami'i ma yasluhu lahu', whether by 'dalalat al-mutabaqah' or by 'dalalat al-tadamun'. Therefore, numerical nouns are not excluded from 'mustaghriq li-jami'i ma yasluhu lahu', and collective nouns like 'rijal', 'muslimun', 'rait', 'qawm' all enter into 'amm. Hence, it was necessary to add the condition of 'non-limited' so that numerical nouns are excluded from it. 'Wa qawlu mustaghriq marfu'' He is adjusting the i'rab of 'mustaghriq': it is marfu' and it is an adjective of the word [i.e., 'amm or lafz], and the meaning of 'istighraq li-ma yasluhu lahu' is that the word indicates all individuals that it is capable of indicating, whether by 'dalalat al-mutabaqah' or by 'dalalat al-tadamun'.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a detailed scholarly commentary on the definition of 'amm (general) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by clarifying the meaning of 'ghayr mahsur' (unlimited) in the definition: it does not mean infinite in reality, but that the word is not accompanied by a contextual indicator (qarina) that specifies a particular number. He then refutes an alternative interpretation that 'ghayr mahsur' means whatever cannot be counted or controlled, using counterexamples like 'al-samawat' (the heavens) which are countable but still considered 'amm by consensus, and 'alf alf' which is not 'amm despite being uncountable. Next, he addresses an objection that the condition 'ghayr mahsur' is redundant (mustadrak) because numerical nouns are already excluded by the condition of istighraq (comprehensiveness). The response explains that numerical nouns like 'mi'a' do possess istighraq in a different way—they indicate all parts of the whole by implication (dalalat al-tadamun)—so they would not be excluded by standard istighraq alone. Therefore, the extra condition 'ghayr mahsur' is necessary to exclude them. Finally, he provides a grammatical note on the word 'mustaghriq' in the definition, confirming it is an adjective modifying the term being defined. Throughout, the commentary follows the order of the base matn (Al-Tawdih) and expands on it using rigorous usul reasoning.

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A general term that includes all individuals it can apply to, provided it is not limited by a contextual indicator.
استغراق (istighrāq): The comprehensiveness of a word to indicate all that it is capable of indicating, whether by dalalat al-mutabaqah or dalalat al-tadamun.
غیر محصور (ghayr maḥṣūr): Not limited; a word that has no contextual indicator specifying a particular number.

Checkpoint
Why is the condition 'ghayr mahsur' necessary in the definition of 'amm?
A) To exclude all plural forms from 'amm.
B) To exclude numerical nouns like mi'a (hundred) from 'amm, because they would not be excluded by istighraq alone.
C) To ensure that 'amm only applies to uncountable nouns.
D) To align the definition with the practice of the Salaf.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'amm requires both comprehensiveness (istighraq) and the absence of numerical limitation (ghayr mahsur); the latter is not redundant but essential to exclude numerical nouns.
